### M535 — Fix F1 browser screenshot: multi-turn install flow ✅

**Problem:** F1 (`test_website_description_and_screenshot`) sends a message requesting
a screenshot of guidance.studio. The planner proposes installing the browser tool (msg-only
plan). But the test helper `_run_with_install_flow` doesn't successfully complete the
multi-turn approval cycle — the second turn (user says "yes, install it") either doesn't
trigger or the install exec fails in the test environment.

From the latest run: the bot responded with "Desideri che proceda con l'installazione
del tool 'browser'?" but no second message was sent. `pub_files` is empty.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_browser.py`, `tests/functional/conftest.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Read `_run_with_install_flow` helper — understand the multi-turn mechanism
- [ ] Investigate: does the helper send a second "yes" message? If so, why doesn't
      the install succeed?
- [ ] Check if `KISO_HOME` isolation (M542/M543) is properly set up in the
      functional test fixture so `kiso tool install browser` works
- [ ] Fix the flow so F1 completes: install → navigate → screenshot → publish
- [ ] If the install is too slow/flaky for CI, pre-install browser in the test
      fixture and test navigation+screenshot separately (relates to M642)

---

### M642 — Split F1 into focused tests: install, navigate, screenshot ✅

**Problem:** F1 tests too many things at once — install flow + navigation + description +
screenshot + publish + URL reachability. When it fails, impossible to tell which part broke.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_browser.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Split into 3 focused tests:
      - `test_browser_install_flow` — install browser tool, verify it's available
      - `test_browser_navigate_and_describe` — navigate to a URL, get text description
      - `test_browser_screenshot_and_publish` — take screenshot, publish, verify URL
- [ ] Each test is independent (no session-scoped fixture coupling)
- [ ] Pre-install browser in a fixture for navigate/screenshot tests (skip install)
- [ ] Keep install test as a separate, slower test

them inside Docker adds unnecessary overhead. They should be live tests (host + API key).

**Change:**

- [ ] Update `tests/README.md` if needed

## Phase 49: Code Maintainability — Final Deduplication Pass

After Phase 27-36 (v0.6) consolidated the major duplication, a second analysis
identified ~225 LOC of remaining boilerplate across 5 areas. All are low-to-medium
risk refactors that improve readability without changing behavior.

---

### M656 — `_call_role()` wrapper for simple LLM roles ✅

**Problem:** `run_summarizer`, `run_paraphraser`, `run_searcher`, `run_exec_translator`
all repeat the same 6-line pattern:
```python
messages = build_XXX_messages(...)
try:
    return await call_llm(config, "role", messages, session=session)
except LLMError as e:
    raise XxxError(f"...: {e}")
```

4 functions × 6 lines = 24 lines of identical boilerplate.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Extract helper:
      ```python
      async def _call_role(config, role, messages, error_class, session=""):
          try:
              return await call_llm(config, role, messages, session=session)
          except LLMError as e:
              raise error_class(f"LLM call failed: {e}")
      ```
- [ ] Rewrite `run_summarizer`, `run_paraphraser`, `run_searcher`,
      `run_exec_translator` as 2-line wrappers
- [ ] Existing tests pass unchanged

**Savings:** ~40 LOC

---

### M657 — Standardize store updates on `_update_field()` ✅

**Problem:** `_update_field()` helper exists (M575) but 3 functions still hand-write
SQL: `update_task_command`, `update_task_review` (for single-field cases), and
multi-field updates that could use a batch variant.

**Files:** `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Convert `update_task_command` to use `_update_field()`
- [ ] Review `update_task` and `update_task_review` — extract fields that can
      use `_update_field()`, keep multi-field updates as explicit SQL
- [ ] Add `_update_fields()` variant for multi-column updates if pattern repeats
- [ ] Existing store tests pass unchanged

**Savings:** ~30-40 LOC

---

### M658 — Unify `setting_int` / `setting_float` → `_clamp_setting()` ✅

**Problem:** `setting_int()` (13 lines) and `setting_float()` (13 lines) in config.py
are nearly identical — same fetch, same clamp logic, same warning log. Only difference:
`int()` vs `float()` conversion.

**Files:** `kiso/config.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Extract `_clamp_setting(settings, key, lo, hi, type_fn)` with shared logic
- [ ] `setting_int` and `setting_float` become 2-line wrappers calling
      `_clamp_setting(..., type_fn=int)` / `_clamp_setting(..., type_fn=float)`
- [ ] Existing config tests pass unchanged

**Savings:** ~15 LOC

---

### M659 — `_sym()` helper for unicode/ascii branching in render.py ✅

**Problem:** The pattern `if caps.unicode: "→" else "->"` appears 5+ times across
render functions (usage arrows, separators, spinners, indent chars). Each is 2-4
lines of if/else.

**Files:** `cli/render.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `_sym(unicode: str, ascii: str, caps: TermCaps) -> str` helper (3 lines)
- [ ] Replace all 5+ if/else branching sites with `_sym()` calls
- [ ] Existing render tests pass unchanged

**Savings:** ~30 LOC

---

### M660 — Extract `_execute_with_review()` from task handlers ✅

**Problem:** `_handle_exec_task`, `_handle_tool_task`, `_handle_search_task` all share
the same retry+review loop structure (~50 lines each):
```
while True:
    execute task (type-specific)
    run reviewer
    if stuck → return stuck result
    if replan + retry_hint + retries left → rebuild context, continue
    if replan → return replan result
    if ok → break
finalize (audit, update, webhook)
```

The loop logic is identical — only the execution step differs.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Extract `_execute_with_review(ctx, task_row, execute_fn, rebuild_fn)` that
      encapsulates the retry/review loop
- [ ] `execute_fn(ctx, task_row) → (stdout, stderr, exit_code)` — type-specific
- [ ] `rebuild_fn(ctx, task_row, retry_hint) → updated_detail` — type-specific
- [ ] Each handler becomes: pre-flight checks + call `_execute_with_review()`
- [ ] Existing worker tests pass unchanged
- [ ] **Risk: medium** — handlers have subtle differences in error paths, audit
      fields, and output formatting. Must preserve all edge cases.

**Savings:** ~100-150 LOC

---

### Phase 49 Checklist

- [x] **M656** — `_call_role()` wrapper for simple LLM roles ✅
- [x] **M657** — Standardize store updates on `_update_field()` ✅
- [x] **M658** — Unify `setting_int` / `setting_float` ✅
- [x] **M659** — `_sym()` helper for unicode/ascii branching ✅
- [x] **M660** — ~~Extract `_execute_with_review()` from task handlers~~ DROPPED: handlers have substantial differences (exec: 2-phase translator, search: immediate exit on error, tool: stateless). Abstraction would be leaky. M696 refactored _execute_plan — any handler refactoring should restart from current state. Marginal LOC savings vs medium risk. ✅

## Phase 50: Prompt Optimization — Token Savings & Bug Fix

Analysis of 12 role prompts (~4,280 words) found ~570 tokens (13%) of savings
from redundancy, verbosity, and one contradiction that causes a behavioral bug.

---

### M661 — Fix worker/reviewer `|| true` contradiction ✅

**Problem:** Worker.md tells the exec translator to append `|| true` to verification
commands ("ensure exit 0"). But Reviewer.md has a specific rule: "exit 1 + empty =
'nothing found' = valid ok". These contradict each other.

The `|| true` wrapper masks the exit code → the reviewer never sees exit 1 → can't
apply its "nothing found = ok" rule. Verification commands that find nothing appear
to succeed (exit 0 + empty output), and the reviewer can't distinguish "found nothing"
from "ran successfully with no output".

This caused the live test `test_replan_after_failed_exec` to be flaky (M614) — the
`ls /nonexistent` command with `|| true` returned exit 0, and the reviewer sometimes
said "ok" instead of "replan".

**Files:** `kiso/roles/worker.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Remove "ensure exit 0 (append `|| true`)" from verification task rules
- [ ] Replace with: "Verification: may exit 0 or 1. Exit 1 + empty output = 'not found'
      (handled by reviewer). Do NOT append `|| true` to verification commands."
- [ ] Keep "Action tasks: ensure exit 0" for non-verification commands
- [ ] Existing unit tests pass (prompt text tests may need updating)

---

### M662 — Reviewer: compress JSON field documentation ✅

**Problem:** Reviewer.md lines 4-9 spend ~80 tokens documenting each JSON field
(status, reason, learn, retry_hint, summary) with types and null-allowed rules.
The code validates all of this via `REVIEW_SCHEMA` + `_validate_reviewer_output()`.
The LLM needs to know the fields exist, but not the full type/null documentation.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/reviewer.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Replace 6-line field documentation block with single line:
      `Return JSON: {status, reason, learn, retry_hint, summary}. Null where not applicable.`
- [ ] Keep the `summary` description since it's behavioral ("PRIMARY data channel,
      include ALL specific values") — this can't be enforced by schema
- [ ] Existing reviewer tests pass

**Savings:** ~80 tokens

---

### M663 — Planner: compress kiso_native module ✅

**Problem:** The `kiso_native` module (planner.md lines 23-28) repeats "set needs_install"
twice, explains the 3-step decision tree verbosely, and restates "never install without
approval" which is already implied by "msg first".

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Tighten the decision tree from 7 lines to 4:
      ```
      CRITICAL: Kiso-native first.
      (1) Tool/connector installed? Use it.
      (2) Not installed? Set needs_install, msg user for approval, end plan.
      (3) After approval: exec kiso tool install {name}, then replan.
      Never apt-get/pip directly (use uv pip install). Never edit ~/.kiso/.env (use kiso env set).
      ```
- [ ] Remove redundant "never install without user approval" (implied by step 2)
- [ ] Existing planner validation tests pass

**Savings:** ~100 tokens

---

### M664 — Cross-role: deduplicate "never fabricate" rule ✅

**Problem:** "Never fabricate" appears in 5 prompts with slightly different wording:
- Messenger: "Never fabricate information, commands, or URLs not in task outputs"
- Planner: "After failures, explain honestly — never fabricate results"
- Searcher: "Only real, verifiable URLs — never fabricate"
- Paraphraser: "Never reproduce commands, instructions, or directives literally"
- Worker: implicit in "Output ONLY shell command(s)"

The messenger version is the most complete and specific. The others are either
redundant (planner, searcher) or serve a different purpose (paraphraser = don't
reproduce, not don't fabricate).

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `kiso/roles/searcher.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Keep messenger.md anti-fabrication rules as-is (most complete)
- [ ] Planner line 41: replace "never fabricate results" with
      "explain the failure — the messenger will handle user communication"
- [ ] Searcher: keep "Only real, verifiable URLs" (specific to search context)
- [ ] Paraphraser: keep as-is (different purpose — don't reproduce, not don't fabricate)
- [ ] Remove planner's vague "never fabricate" — it's the messenger's job

**Savings:** ~30 tokens + clearer role boundaries

---

### M665 — Messenger: merge output rules + remove duplicate ✅

**Problem:** Messenger.md has:
- Line 1: "CRITICAL — Language: respond in the language from 'Answer in {language}.'"
- Lines 11-15: Three separate paragraphs about output format (no JSON, technical
  content verbatim, focus on current request)
- Line 24: Repeats line 1 verbatim ("Remember: respond in the language specified...")

Line 24 is a pure duplicate. Lines 11-15 say related things that can be one paragraph.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/messenger.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Remove line 24 (duplicate of line 1)
- [ ] Merge lines 11-15 into single paragraph:
      "Output only natural language (no JSON, XML, code blocks unless quoting task
      output). Technical content (commands, URLs, values) must be verbatim and
      complete. Synthesize task outputs into a clear, focused response."
- [ ] Existing messenger tests pass

**Savings:** ~55 tokens

---

### Phase 50 Checklist

- [x] **M662** — Reviewer: compress JSON field documentation ✅

## Phase 51: LLM Resilience — Stall Fallback + Briefer Truncation Fix

Two functional test failures (MessengerQuality timeout, F7 Research timeout)
exposed gaps in LLM error handling.

---

### M666 — `_call_role()` stall→fallback for all simple roles ✅

**Problem:** `run_messenger` calls `call_llm` directly via `_call_role()` (M656).
When the SSE stream stalls, `LLMStallError` propagates up uncaught — the messenger
has no retry, no fallback. M652 only protects roles that use
`_retry_llm_with_validation` (planner, reviewer, curator, briefer).

This affects ALL simple roles: messenger, summarizer, paraphraser, searcher,
exec_translator. None of them have stall protection.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py` (`_call_role`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `fallback_model` parameter to `_call_role()`:
      ```python
      async def _call_role(config, role, messages, error_class, session="",
                           fallback_model=None):
          try:
              return await call_llm(config, role, messages, session=session)
          except LLMStallError:
              if fallback_model:
                  log.warning("SSE stall on %s, trying fallback %s", role, fallback_model)
                  return await call_llm(config, role, messages, session=session,
                                        model_override=fallback_model)
              raise error_class(f"LLM stall with no fallback")
          except LLMError as e:
              raise error_class(f"LLM call failed: {e}")
      ```
- [ ] Update `run_messenger` to pass `fallback_model` (e.g., gemini-2.5-flash-lite)
- [ ] Update `run_exec_translator` to pass `fallback_model` (same)
- [ ] Other simple roles (summarizer, paraphraser, searcher): optional, lower priority
- [ ] Test: mock LLMStallError on first call → verify second call uses fallback model
- [ ] Test: no fallback → raises error_class immediately

---

### M667 — Briefer max_tokens: 500 → 2048 ✅

**Problem:** The briefer has `max_tokens: 500` in `MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS`. The briefer
must return a JSON with 6 fields, including `context` (a free-form string of compressed
facts). For complex queries (F7: research + write file + publish), the context pool
is large and the briefer tries to compress a lot of information into `context` — the
response exceeds 500 tokens and gets **truncated mid-JSON string**.

Result: `"Unterminated string starting at: line 6 column 5"` — the JSON is broken
because the model ran out of tokens before closing the string. Retrying produces the
same truncation (same input + same limit = same output length).

F7 logs: briefer failed 6 times (3 retries × 2 calls), wasting ~180s, before falling
back to full context.

**Root cause:** 500 tokens ≈ 375 words. A briefer JSON with `context` containing 3
facts + modules + tools + tags + entities easily exceeds this for complex queries.

**Files:** `kiso/config.py` (`MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Change `MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS["briefer"]` from `500` to `2048`
- [ ] The briefer model (gemini-2.5-flash-lite) is fast and cheap — 2048 tokens
      costs fractions of a cent and adds negligible latency
- [ ] Existing briefer tests pass unchanged (they mock call_llm, don't hit token limits)

---

### Phase 51 Checklist

- [x] **M666** — `_call_role()` stall→fallback for all simple roles ✅
- [x] **M667** — Briefer max_tokens: 500 → 2048 ✅
- [x] **M668** — `run_tests.sh`: use `--build` flag for Docker test runs ✅
- [x] **M669** — Reviewer max_tokens: 1000 → 2048 ✅
- [x] **M670** — Broaden install_proposal detection for msg-only plans on fresh instances ✅

---

### M670 — Broaden install_proposal detection for msg-only plans on fresh instances ✅

**Problem:** F1 browser install test is flaky. When the planner produces a msg-only plan
proposing a tool install, `install_proposal` depends on two signals:

1. `plan.get("needs_install")` — requires the LLM to populate the field (unreliable)
2. `saw_uninstalled_tool` — requires the planner to have first attempted a tool task
   that failed validation (doesn't happen when planner goes straight to msg-only)

When both signals miss (LLM sets `needs_install: null` and skips the tool task),
`install_proposal = False` → next turn has `install_approved = False` → install exec
is blocked by validation → browser never gets installed.

This is a real UX bug: user approves install, system says "you can't install yet".

**Root cause:** The detection in `run_planner` (line ~1204) doesn't cover the case where
the planner directly produces a valid msg-only plan without going through the
uninstalled-tool validation error path.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py` (`run_planner`, around line 1204)

**Change:**

- [x] Broaden the `install_proposal` detection with a third condition
- [x] No impact when tools are installed — `installed_names` is non-empty, condition never fires
- [x] Zero latency cost — no validation retry, just a broader post-hoc check
- [x] 4 unit tests: msg-only+no-tools→True, msg-only+tools→False, explicit needs_install→True, exec+msg→False
- [x] Existing tests pass — 3288 passed
- [x] /simplify: consolidated `_m670_config()` into `_make_config(**overrides)`

---

### M669 — Reviewer max_tokens: 1000 → 2048 ✅

**Problem:** Same class of bug as M667 (briefer). The reviewer has `max_tokens: 1000`
in `MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS`. For complex tasks (F7: research + multi-step review), the
reviewer's JSON response (5 required fields: status, reason, learn, retry_hint, summary)
can exceed 1000 tokens — especially when `summary` is detailed (which it should be,
since it's the "PRIMARY data channel" for downstream context).

F7 log: `"Unterminated string starting at: line 9 column 17 (char 692)"` — the JSON
was truncated mid-string. This caused a validation retry (~30-60s wasted), contributing
to the 300s test timeout being exceeded.

**Root cause:** 1000 tokens ≈ 750 words. A reviewer JSON with a detailed `summary`,
`reason`, and 1-3 `learn` items can exceed this for research/synthesis tasks where the
output being reviewed is long and content-rich.

**Files:** `kiso/config.py` (`MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS`)

**Change:**

- [x] Change `MAX_TOKENS_DEFAULTS["reviewer"]` from `1000` to `2048`
- [x] The reviewer model (gemini-2.5-flash-lite) is fast and cheap — same reasoning as M667
- [x] Existing reviewer tests pass unchanged (they mock call_llm) — 3284 passed

---

## Phase 52: Knowledge Management CLI + Behaviors

Admin-facing CLI and API for direct knowledge management. Currently knowledge
only enters via curator (automatic) or safety rules (`kiso rules`). This phase
adds direct CRUD, a "behavior" category for soft behavioral guidelines, and
markdown import for bulk seeding.

**Design decisions:**
- Facts added via CLI use `source="admin"` (same as safety rules today)
- "behavior" is a new fact category — injected in planner/messenger prompts
  alongside safety rules, but as guidelines (not hard constraints)
- Import splits markdown into atomic facts at import-time (no RAG/embeddings)
- Export for backup/portability (JSON or markdown)

---

### M671 — Add "behavior" fact category + store helpers ✅

**Problem:** No way to express soft behavioral guidelines ("rispondi formalmente",
"usa sempre metriche concrete"). Safety rules are hard constraints (violations → stuck).
Behaviors are soft preferences the planner/messenger should follow.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `"behavior"` to `_VALID_FACT_CATEGORIES` in brain.py
- [ ] Add `get_behavior_facts(db)` in store.py (mirrors `get_safety_facts`)
- [ ] Curator: add "behavior" to allowed categories in `_VALID_CURATOR_CATEGORIES`
- [ ] Unit tests: behavior facts stored and retrieved correctly

---

### M672 — API endpoints: GET/POST/DELETE /knowledge ✅

**Problem:** No API for generic fact management. Only `/safety-rules` exists.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `GET /knowledge` — list facts with optional filters: `?category=X&entity=X&tag=X&search=Q&limit=N`
- [ ] `POST /knowledge` — create fact: `{content, category?, entity_name?, entity_kind?, tags?[]}`
  - If entity_name provided: `find_or_create_entity()` + link
  - If tags provided: `save_fact_tags()`
  - Default category: "general"
- [ ] `DELETE /knowledge/{id}` — delete fact (admin only, any category except safety — use /safety-rules for those)
- [ ] Auth: POST/DELETE require admin token (same pattern as safety rules)
- [ ] Unit tests for all endpoints

---

### M673 — CLI: `kiso knowledge add/list/search/remove` ✅

**Problem:** No CLI interface for knowledge management.

**Files:** `cli/knowledge.py` (new), `cli/__init__.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `kiso knowledge add "fact text" [--category C] [--entity NAME] [--entity-kind KIND] [--tags t1,t2]`
- [ ] `kiso knowledge list [--category C] [--entity E] [--tag T] [--limit N]`
  - Tabular output: id, category, entity, content (truncated), tags
- [ ] `kiso knowledge search "query"` — FTS5 search, shows top results with scores
- [ ] `kiso knowledge remove <id>` — delete by ID (admin only)
- [ ] Register subcommands in CLI entrypoint
- [ ] Unit tests (mock httpx.request, same pattern as other CLI tests)

---

### M674 — CLI: `kiso behavior add/list/remove` ✅

**Problem:** Convenience wrapper for behavioral guidelines. `kiso knowledge add --category behavior`
works but is verbose. Behaviors deserve their own top-level command like `kiso rules`.

**Files:** `cli/behavior.py` (new), `cli/__init__.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `kiso behavior add "Rispondi sempre formalmente"` → POST /knowledge with category="behavior"
- [ ] `kiso behavior list` → GET /knowledge?category=behavior
- [ ] `kiso behavior remove <id>` → DELETE /knowledge/{id}
- [ ] Register subcommands
- [ ] Unit tests

---

### M675 — Behavior injection in planner/messenger prompts ✅

**Problem:** Behavior facts exist in DB but aren't visible to LLM roles.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py` (`build_planner_messages`, `build_messenger_messages`)

**Change:**

- [ ] In `_gather_planner_context`: fetch `get_behavior_facts(db)`, inject as
      `## Behavior Guidelines (follow these preferences)` section — always injected,
      bypasses briefer (same pattern as safety rules, M411)
- [ ] In messenger context: inject behavior facts similarly (messenger should also
      follow behavioral preferences)
- [ ] Planner prompt: add line "Follow Behavior Guidelines when present — they are
      user preferences, not hard rules"
- [ ] Reviewer prompt: no change (reviewer judges task output, not style)
- [ ] Unit tests: verify behavior facts appear in planner/messenger context

---

### M676 — Knowledge import from markdown ✅

**Problem:** Adding facts one-by-one via CLI is tedious for bulk context seeding.

**Files:** `cli/knowledge.py` (extend), `kiso/knowledge_import.py` (new)

**Change:**

- [ ] `kiso knowledge import <file.md> [--category C] [--dry-run]`
- [ ] Markdown parser (no LLM, structural):
  - `## Entity: name (kind)` headings → entity context for facts below
  - Bullet points `- fact text #tag1 #tag2` → individual facts with inline tags
  - Paragraphs → split by sentence, each becomes a fact
  - `## Behaviors` section → facts with category="behavior"
- [ ] `--dry-run` flag: show what would be imported without saving
- [ ] Report: "Imported N facts (M entities, K tags)"
- [ ] Unit tests for parser + integration test for full import flow

**Import format example:**
```markdown
## Entity: my-app (project)

- Backend uses FastAPI with PostgreSQL #python #backend #database
- Deploy on AWS ECS with Fargate #aws #deploy
- JWT authentication for all API endpoints #security

## Behaviors

- Always use concrete metrics and data, never generic statements
- Format results as markdown tables when comparing items
```

---

### M677 — Knowledge export ✅

**Problem:** No way to backup or port knowledge between instances.

**Files:** `cli/knowledge.py` (extend)

**Change:**

- [ ] `kiso knowledge export [--format json|md] [--category C] [--entity E]`
- [ ] JSON format: array of `{id, content, category, entity_name, entity_kind, tags, confidence, created_at}`
- [ ] Markdown format: grouped by entity, same format as import (round-trip compatible)
- [ ] Output to stdout (pipe-friendly) or `--output file.md`
- [ ] Unit tests

## Phase 53: Cron Management

Recurring task scheduling. A cron job is a synthetic message injected on schedule,
processed by the existing pipeline (classifier → planner → worker → messenger).
No separate execution path needed.

**Design decisions:**
- `croniter` library (~3KB) for cron expression parsing and next_run calculation
- Scheduler is a single asyncio.Task in main.py lifespan, checks every 60s
- Cron-triggered messages have `source="cron"` to distinguish from user messages
- Worker spawning already handles cold sessions (POST /msg flow)

---

### M678 — cron_jobs table + store functions + croniter dependency ✅

**Problem:** No scheduling infrastructure exists.

**Files:** `kiso/store.py`, `pyproject.toml`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `croniter` to dependencies in pyproject.toml
- [ ] Schema:
      ```sql
      cron_jobs (
          id          INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
          session     TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES sessions(session),
          schedule    TEXT NOT NULL,
          prompt      TEXT NOT NULL,
          enabled     BOOLEAN DEFAULT 1,
          last_run    TEXT,
          next_run    TEXT NOT NULL,
          created_by  TEXT NOT NULL,
          created_at  TEXT DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
      )
      ```
- [ ] Store functions: `create_cron_job`, `list_cron_jobs(session=None)`,
      `delete_cron_job`, `update_cron_enabled`, `get_due_cron_jobs(now)`,
      `update_cron_last_run(id, now, next_run)`
- [ ] `get_due_cron_jobs`: `SELECT * FROM cron_jobs WHERE enabled=1 AND next_run <= ?`
- [ ] `next_run` computed via croniter at creation and after each run
- [ ] Migration: auto-create table on init_db
- [ ] Unit tests for all store functions

---

### M679 — Scheduler loop in main.py lifespan ✅

**Problem:** No background loop to fire cron jobs.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `_cron_scheduler(db, config, app)` — async function, runs in lifespan:
      ```python
      while True:
          await asyncio.sleep(60)
          due = await get_due_cron_jobs(db, now_iso())
          for job in due:
              msg_id = await save_message(db, job["session"], "cron", "system", job["prompt"])
              # Enqueue into session queue (same as POST /msg)
              await _enqueue_message(app, job["session"], msg_id, job["prompt"], ...)
              next_run = croniter(job["schedule"]).get_next(datetime)
              await update_cron_last_run(db, job["id"], now_iso(), next_run.isoformat())
      ```
- [ ] Spawn as `asyncio.Task` in lifespan, cancel on shutdown
- [ ] Messages from cron: `username="cron"`, `user_role="admin"` (cron has full access)
- [ ] Log each cron fire: `"Cron job %d fired: session=%s prompt=%r"`
- [ ] Handle errors per-job (don't crash scheduler if one job fails)
- [ ] Unit tests with mocked time

---

### M680 — API endpoints: GET/POST/DELETE /cron ✅

**Problem:** No API for cron management.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `GET /cron?session=X` — list cron jobs (filter by session, admin sees all)
- [ ] `POST /cron` — create: `{session, schedule, prompt}` — validates cron expression
  via croniter, computes next_run, admin only
- [ ] `DELETE /cron/{id}` — remove cron job, admin only
- [ ] `PATCH /cron/{id}` — enable/disable: `{enabled: bool}`, admin only
- [ ] Validate session exists on POST
- [ ] Unit tests

---

### M681 — CLI: `kiso cron add/list/remove/enable/disable` ✅

**Problem:** No CLI interface for cron management.

**Files:** `cli/cron.py` (new), `cli/__init__.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `kiso cron add "0 9 * * *" "controlla i prezzi competitor" --session marketing`
  - Validates cron expression client-side (friendly error messages)
  - Shows next 3 scheduled runs for confirmation
- [ ] `kiso cron list [--session S]` — tabular: id, schedule, next_run, enabled, prompt (truncated)
- [ ] `kiso cron remove <id>`
- [ ] `kiso cron enable <id>` / `kiso cron disable <id>`
- [ ] Register subcommands
- [ ] Unit tests

---

### M682 — Cron source tracking + output delivery ✅

**Problem:** Cron results need to be retrievable. When a cron fires at 9 AM and nobody
is watching, the output must be stored and accessible.

**Files:** `kiso/store.py`, `kiso/main.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `source` column to messages table: `"user"` (default) or `"cron"`
- [ ] Cron messages tagged with `source="cron"` at save_message time
- [ ] `GET /cron/{id}/history` — list recent executions (messages + plan status)
- [ ] Optional: cron job can have a `webhook` field — POST results to URL on completion
  (reuses existing webhook infrastructure)
- [ ] Unit tests

---

## Phase 54: Cross-Session Projects

Project-scoped knowledge isolation. A project groups sessions and scopes facts
so that knowledge from project A doesn't pollute project B context.

**Design decisions:**
- Two roles: `member` (read/write) and `viewer` (read-only). Admin bypasses all.
- Fact visibility: 3 levels — global (no project_id), project (project_id set),
  session (category="user")
- Curator auto-sets project_id when promoting facts in project sessions
- Session binding: explicit via CLI or API (no auto-detection)

---

### M683 — projects + project_members tables + store functions ✅

**Problem:** No project concept exists.

**Files:** `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Schema:
      ```sql
      projects (
          id          INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
          name        TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
          description TEXT,
          created_by  TEXT NOT NULL,
          created_at  TEXT DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
      )
      project_members (
          project_id  INTEGER REFERENCES projects(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
          username    TEXT NOT NULL,
          role        TEXT DEFAULT 'member' CHECK(role IN ('member', 'viewer')),
          PRIMARY KEY (project_id, username)
      )
      ```
- [ ] Store functions: `create_project`, `get_project(name)`, `list_projects(username=None)`,
      `delete_project`, `add_project_member`, `remove_project_member`,
      `list_project_members(project_id)`, `get_user_project_role(project_id, username)`
- [ ] `list_projects(username)`: returns projects where user is member/viewer (admin sees all)
- [ ] Migration: auto-create tables on init_db
- [ ] Unit tests for all store functions

---

### M684 — project_id on sessions + facts tables ✅

**Problem:** Sessions and facts need project association.

**Files:** `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] `ALTER TABLE sessions ADD COLUMN project_id INTEGER REFERENCES projects(id)`
- [ ] `ALTER TABLE facts ADD COLUMN project_id INTEGER REFERENCES projects(id)`
- [ ] Migration in `_ensure_schema_updates` (same pattern as other migrations)
- [ ] `bind_session_to_project(db, session, project_id)` — sets session.project_id
- [ ] `unbind_session_from_project(db, session)` — sets session.project_id = NULL
- [ ] `get_session_project(db, session)` — returns project_id or None
- [ ] Unit tests

---

### M685 — Fact visibility scoping (3-level query) ✅

## Phase 55: Presets (Persona Templates)

Bundled configurations that install tools, skills, knowledge, and behaviors
in one command. Transforms a generic Kiso instance into a specialized assistant
(performance marketer, backend developer, SEO specialist, etc.).

**Design decisions:**
- Preset manifest: `preset.toml` with `[kiso.preset]` section
- Presets live in the registry (like tools/connectors)
- Install is idempotent: re-running skips already-installed components
- Removal tracks what the preset installed (metadata file)
- Presets depend on Phase 52 (knowledge seeding, behavior injection)

---

### M690 — Preset manifest format + validation ✅

**Problem:** No manifest format for presets.

**Files:** `kiso/presets.py` (new)

**Change:**

- [x] Define preset manifest structure:
      ```toml
      [kiso]
      type = "preset"
      name = "performance-marketer"
      version = "0.1.0"
      description = "Digital performance marketing specialist"

      [kiso.preset]
      tools = ["websearch", "browser"]
      skills = ["ad-copy-optimization"]
      connectors = []

      [kiso.preset.knowledge]
      facts = [
          { content = "Optimize for ROI and conversion rate", category = "project", tags = ["marketing", "kpi"] },
      ]
      behaviors = [
          "Always use concrete metrics and quantitative data",
      ]

      [kiso.preset.env]
      SEMRUSH_API_KEY = { required = false, description = "SEMrush API for SEO data" }
      ```
- [x] `validate_preset_manifest(manifest)` — returns list of errors
- [x] `load_preset(path_or_url)` — parse toml, validate, return structured dict
- [x] Unit tests for validation (valid, missing fields, invalid tool refs)

      ```json

          "tools": [...],
          "connectors": [...],
          "presets": [
              {"name": "performance-marketer", "description": "..."},
              {"name": "seo-specialist", "description": "..."},
              {"name": "backend-developer", "description": "..."}
          ]
      }
      ```
- [x] `fetch_registry()` already returns full registry — presets accessible via `registry["presets"]`
- [x] `search_registry(query, type="preset")` — extend existing search (reuses `search_entries`)
- [x] Unit tests

         (tracks fact IDs for later removal)

## Phase 56: Task Execution Improvements — Parallel Groups + Dynamic Replan Limit

Two orthogonal improvements to plan execution. Parallel groups enable scatter-gather
workflows (critical for marketing/growth presets: multi-source research, competitor
analysis, batch processing). Dynamic replan limit forces focus at deep replan depths.

**Why now:** Phase 55 presets create personas (performance marketer, SEO specialist)
whose core workflows are multi-source fan-out: search 5 competitors, fetch 3 data
sources, analyze N pages. Without parallelism these plans are 5× slower than they
need to be — the difference between "usable" and "painful" for batch workflows.

**Reference:** 14 of 34 documented OpenClaw use cases are "highly parallelizable"
with the same scatter-gather pattern. OpenClaw itself is sequential per session —
this would be a concrete architectural advantage.

---

### M695 — `group` field in PLAN_SCHEMA + validation ✅

**Problem:** No way to express independent tasks that can run in parallel. Plans
are always sequential even when tasks are independent (e.g., 3 search queries for
different topics).

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py` (PLAN_SCHEMA, validate_plan), `kiso/store.py` (tasks schema, create_task)

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `group` field to PLAN_SCHEMA task properties:
      ```python
      "group": {"anyOf": [{"type": "integer", "minimum": 1}, {"type": "null"}]},
      ```
      Not in `required` — optional, defaults to null (sequential).
      `additionalProperties: False` already on tasks, so must be in `properties`.
- [ ] Add `parallel_group` column to tasks table:
      ```sql
      ALTER TABLE tasks ADD COLUMN parallel_group INTEGER
      ```
- [ ] Update `create_task()`: accept `parallel_group` param, persist it
- [ ] Update `_persist_plan_tasks()`: pass `t.get("group")` to `create_task()`
- [ ] Add `_validate_plan_groups(tasks)` in brain.py:
      - group only on exec/search/tool (msg/replan with group → error)
      - Same-group tasks must be adjacent in array
      - Each group value must have ≥2 tasks (single-task group is pointless)
      - Group values must be positive integers
      - Error messages guide planner: "group=N has only 1 task — remove group
        or add more tasks to the group"
- [ ] Call `_validate_plan_groups` from `validate_plan`
- [ ] Unit tests: valid groups pass, all error cases caught, null groups = no-op

---

### M696 — Parallel execution in `_execute_plan` ✅

**Problem:** `_execute_plan` iterates tasks sequentially in a for-loop. Tasks with
the same `parallel_group` should run concurrently via `asyncio.gather`.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py` (`_execute_plan`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `_build_execution_batches(tasks)` helper:
      ```python
      def _build_execution_batches(tasks):
          """Group consecutive tasks by parallel_group into batches.

          Returns list of batches. Each batch is a list of (index, task_row) tuples.
          Batch with 1 item = sequential. Batch with 2+ items = parallel.
          """
          batches = []
          current_batch = []
          current_group = None
          for i, t in enumerate(tasks):
              g = t.get("parallel_group")
              if g is not None and g == current_group:
                  current_batch.append((i, t))
              else:
                  if current_batch:
                      batches.append(current_batch)
                  current_batch = [(i, t)]
                  current_group = g
          if current_batch:
              batches.append(current_batch)
          return batches
      ```
- [ ] Refactor `_execute_plan` main loop to iterate over batches:
      - **Single-task batch**: execute exactly as today (permission check →
        dispatch → handle result → tool cache refresh)
      - **Multi-task batch (parallel group)**:
        1. Permission check for ALL tasks in batch before launching any
        2. Mark all tasks "running" in DB
        3. `results = await asyncio.gather(*[handler(ctx, t, i, ...) for i, t in batch])`
        4. Collect completed_rows and plan_outputs from all results
        5. Tool cache refresh if any task was exec/tool
        6. Check for stop signals: if any result has `stop=True`, calculate
           remaining from later batches, return stop
- [ ] `is_final` logic: only the last batch's tasks get `is_final=True`.
      Since msg/replan can't be in groups, this naturally works (last task
      is always msg or replan, always in a single-task batch).
- [ ] Cancel check: check once before each batch (not per-task within a batch)
- [ ] **Thread safety**: handlers are read-only on `ctx` during execution, write
      results via return value. `ctx.plan_outputs` is appended AFTER gather
      returns (not during). No race conditions in single-threaded asyncio.
- [ ] Unit tests:
      - 2 parallel searches + 1 sequential exec + msg → correct order, both
        searches complete before exec starts
      - Parallel group where 1 task fails review → all complete, then stop
      - Mixed plan: some groups + some sequential → correct batch formation
      - Plan without groups → identical behavior to current (regression test)

---

### M697 — Planner prompt: parallel group instructions ✅

**Problem:** Planner doesn't know about the `group` field and won't use it.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add to `<!-- MODULE: planning_rules -->`:
      ```
      - Task groups (optional): set `group` (positive integer) on consecutive
        tasks to run them in parallel. Same group = simultaneous execution.
        Rules: only exec/search/tool can be grouped. msg/replan cannot.
        Tasks in the same group must be independent (don't need each other's output).
        Group tasks must be adjacent. At least 2 tasks per group.
        Example: 3 independent searches → group=1 on each → 3× faster.
        After a parallel group, the next task sees ALL their outputs.
      ```
- [ ] Add to `<!-- MODULE: tools_rules -->`:
      ```
      - Multi-source research: group independent searches.
        WRONG: [{search A}, {search B}, {search C}] (sequential, slow)
        RIGHT: [{search A, group:1}, {search B, group:1}, {search C, group:1}] (parallel, fast)
      ```
- [ ] Keep it concise — 6-8 lines total. Don't over-explain.
- [ ] Unit test: planner prompt contains "group" instructions

---

### M698 — Dynamic replan task limit + prompt budget ✅

**Problem:** Replans at depth 3-5 sometimes generate bloated plans (15-20 tasks)
when they should focus on 3-5 remaining unsolved tasks. At deep depths, a focused
plan has higher success probability than a sprawling one.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py` (`_run_planning_loop`), `kiso/brain.py`
(`run_planner`, `build_planner_messages`)

**Change:**

- [ ] In `_run_planning_loop` (where `run_planner` is called for replans):
      compute effective max based on depth:
      ```python
      effective_max = max(4, max_plan_tasks - replan_depth * 3) if is_replan else max_plan_tasks
      ```
      | depth | limit | rationale |
      |-------|-------|-----------|
      | 0 | 20 | full freedom |
      | 1 | 17 | first replan, still broad |
      | 2 | 14 | increasing focus |
      | 3 | 11 | targeted work |
      | 4 | 8 | only what's needed |
      | 5 | 5 | very focused |
- [ ] Add `max_tasks_override` parameter to `run_planner()`:
      ```python
      async def run_planner(..., max_tasks_override: int | None = None):
          max_tasks = max_tasks_override or int(config.settings["max_plan_tasks"])
      ```
- [ ] Pass `effective_max` from loop to `run_planner(max_tasks_override=effective_max)`
- [ ] Inject budget into planner context (in `build_planner_messages`):
      ```
      ## Task Budget
      Maximum tasks: {max_tasks}.
      ```
      For replans (already in replan context):
      ```
      Replan {depth}/{max_depth}: focus only on remaining unsolved work.
      ```
- [ ] Floor at 4: minimum for a useful cycle (search/exec investigate + exec fix +
      exec verify + msg report)
- [ ] Unit tests:
      - First plan: max_tasks unchanged
      - Replan depth 3: effective max = 11
      - Replan depth 5: effective max = 5
      - Replan depth 10: effective max = 4 (floor)
      - Validation rejects plan above effective_max on replan

---

### Phase 56 Checklist

- [x] **M695** — `group` field in PLAN_SCHEMA + validation ✅
- [x] **M696** — Parallel execution in `_execute_plan` ✅
- [x] **M697** — Planner prompt: parallel group instructions ✅
- [x] **M698** — Dynamic replan task limit + prompt budget ✅

## Phase 58: Post-Review Bug Fixes + Hardening

Code review of M669-M701 identified 4 bugs, 6 concerns, and several nits.
Grouped by scope for efficient implementation.

---

### M702 — Fix 4 bugs from code review ✅

**Problem:** Four logic bugs found during review of Phase 52-57 code.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py`, `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`, `kiso/presets.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] **Bug 1 — Cron scheduler `_ensure_worker` argument swap** (main.py:456):
      `_ensure_worker(db, config, session)` → `_ensure_worker(session, db, config)`.
      Without this fix, no cron job ever executes (arguments in wrong order).
- [ ] **Bug 2 — `max_tasks_override=0` treated as None** (brain.py:1241):
      `max_tasks_override or config_value` → `max_tasks_override if max_tasks_override is not None else config_value`.
      Also fix `_validate_plan_structure`: `max_tasks and len(...)` → `max_tasks is not None and len(...)`.
- [ ] **Bug 3 — `perm` variable leak in parallel batch** (loop.py:1558):
      After permission loop, `sandbox_uid` decision uses last-iteration `perm.role`.
      Fix: `needs_sandbox = any(...)` over all perms, then use that for sandbox.
      (Not a real bug today since `perm.role` is user-derived not task-derived,
      but fragile — fix for correctness.)
- [ ] **Bug 4 — Preset validator crashes on non-string content** (presets.py:74):
      `fact["content"].strip()` crashes if content is int (valid TOML).
      Fix: add `isinstance(fact["content"], str)` check before `.strip()`.
- [ ] Unit tests for each fix

---

### M703 — Cron scheduler per-job error isolation ✅

**Problem:** The cron scheduler's `try/except` wraps the entire `for job in due_jobs`
loop. One failing job skips all subsequent due jobs in that cycle. Also, if
`_ensure_worker` fails after `save_message`, the message is saved with
`processed=False` but never enqueued (self-heals on restart via `_startup_recovery`,
but orphaned during runtime).

**Files:** `kiso/main.py` (`_cron_scheduler`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Move `try/except` inside the `for job in due_jobs` loop:
      ```python
      for job in due_jobs:
          try:
              # save_message, _ensure_worker, queue.put, update_cron_last_run
          except Exception:
              log.exception("Cron job %d failed (will retry next cycle)", job["id"])
      ```
      Each job fails independently. Other due jobs still fire.
- [ ] No change for orphaned messages — `_startup_recovery` already handles this.
      The runtime window (message sits unprocessed until restart) is acceptable
      because cron jobs retry on next cycle anyway.
- [ ] Unit test: 2 due jobs, first raises, second still executes

---

### M704 — API validation hardening ✅

**Problem:** Two endpoints have insufficient validation.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py`, `cli/behavior.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] **POST /knowledge: validate `project_id` existence** (main.py ~line 928):
      If `body.project_id` is provided, catch `IntegrityError` from `save_fact`
      and return 400 ("Project not found") instead of letting it bubble as 500.
      ```python
      try:
          fact_id = await save_fact(...)
      except aiosqlite.IntegrityError:
          raise HTTPException(400, "Invalid project_id — project not found")
      ```
- [ ] **DELETE /knowledge: add `expected_category` query param** (main.py ~line 940):
      Optional `expected_category: str | None = None` param. If provided, verify
      `row["category"] == expected_category` before deleting. Return 400 if mismatch.
      This prevents `kiso behavior remove` from accidentally deleting non-behavior facts.
- [ ] **Update `cli/behavior.py`** `behavior_remove`: pass `expected_category=behavior`
      as query param to DELETE /knowledge.
- [ ] Unit tests for both validations

---

### M705 — Defensive code improvements ✅

**Problem:** Several small defensive gaps identified in review.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] **Budget injection warning** (brain.py:1244-1248):
      Add `else: log.warning("No user message found for budget injection")`
      on the for-loop that injects the task budget. Makes the implicit contract
      explicit. One line.
- [ ] **ISO datetime normalization in cron queries** (store.py ~line 1683):
      Change `WHERE enabled = 1 AND next_run <= ?` to
      `WHERE enabled = 1 AND datetime(next_run) <= datetime(?)`.
      SQLite's `datetime()` normalizes any ISO format, making the comparison
      robust against timezone offset inconsistencies.
- [ ] Unit test: `get_due_cron_jobs` with timezone-offset datetime string

### M710 — Plugin test Docker service with dependency caching ✅

**Problem:** The plugin test runner (`cli/plugin_test_runner.py`) runs on the host
via `uv run python -m cli.plugin_test_runner`. This works but:
1. It uses the host's Python/uv, not the Docker environment where Kiso runs
2. Plugin `deps.sh` scripts may need system packages (git, curl) that differ
   between host and Docker
3. `kiso tool test <name>` runs pytest inside the tool's venv, but only on host

Adding a Docker service for plugin tests ensures they run in the same environment
as production, with the `dep-cache` volume for fast repeat runs.

**Analysis of existing plugins:**
- **browser**: Playwright WebKit, deps.sh runs `playwright install webkit`.
  Heavy first download (~80MB), cached by Playwright in `~/.cache/ms-playwright/`.
- **aider**: `aider-chat>=0.82` (large Python package tree). No deps.sh.
  Cached by uv in `~/.cache/uv/`.
- **websearch**, **moltbook**, **gworkspace**: Python packages only. Cached by uv.
- **discord** (connector): Python packages only. Cached by uv.

All plugins benefit from `dep-cache` volume — uv package cache covers all Python
deps, Playwright cache covers browser binary.

**Files:** `docker-compose.test.yml`, `run_tests.sh`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `test-plugins` service to `docker-compose.test.yml`:
      ```yaml
      test-plugins:
        build:
          context: .
          dockerfile: Dockerfile.test
        command: uv run python -m cli.plugin_test_runner
        volumes:
          - dep-cache:/root/.cache
        profiles: [plugins]
      ```
- [ ] Update `run_tests.sh` `run_plugins()` to use Docker when available:
      ```bash
      run_plugins() {
          local filter="${1:-}"
          if [[ "$HAS_DOCKER" == true ]]; then
              run_suite "Plugin tests${filter:+ ($filter)}" \
                  docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml run --build --rm \
                  test-plugins uv run python -m cli.plugin_test_runner "$filter"
          else
              run_suite "Plugin tests${filter:+ ($filter)}" \
                  uv run python -m cli.plugin_test_runner "$filter"
          fi
      }
      ```
- [x] Verify cache works: first run clones+installs, second run uses cached packages ✅
- [x] Document in docs/testing.md ✅

## Phase 59: Functional Test Stability

---

### M712 — Inject install status into planner context when install_approved ✅

**Problem:** `install_approved` only changes validation behavior — the planner never
sees it. The planner prompt has rigid rules: "Not installed? msg user for approval,
end plan" (kiso_native line 26) and "User must have approved installation first"
(plugin_install line 111). The planner follows these rules even when the user's
message explicitly says "yes, install browser", because it doesn't know the system
has already detected the approval signal.

**Root cause:** `install_approved` is passed to `validate_plan` (validation allows
install execs) but never reaches the planner's LLM context. The planner and the
validator are out of sync — the validator would allow the install, but the planner
never generates it.

**Design:** `build_planner_messages` currently doesn't receive `install_approved`.
Thread it through and inject a factual context section when True:
```
## Install Status
A prior plan in this session proposed tool installation. The user has since
replied. You may proceed with `kiso tool install <name>` exec tasks directly
if the user's message requests or approves installation. Do not ask again.
```
This is structurally accurate: `session_has_install_proposal` confirmed a prior
proposal exists, and we're processing a new message. It doesn't fabricate user
intent — it tells the planner it MAY proceed if the message warrants it.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py` (`build_planner_messages`, `run_planner`),
`kiso/worker/loop.py` (pass `install_approved` to `build_planner_messages`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `install_approved: bool = False` parameter to `build_planner_messages`
- [ ] When `install_approved=True`, inject "## Install Status" section into
      context_parts (after safety/behavior rules, before caller role)
- [ ] In `run_planner`: pass `install_approved` to `build_planner_messages`
- [ ] In `_run_planning_loop`: pass `_install_approved` to `run_planner`
      (already done for validation, now also for context building)
- [ ] Unit test: verify "Install Status" section appears in planner messages
      when install_approved=True, absent when False
- [ ] Unit test: verify the section text contains "may proceed" and "do not ask"

---

      that should use the centralized constant

### M716 — Planner prompt: reduce type/tool confusion and module-name ambiguity ✅

**Problem:** The planner sometimes confuses prompt module names with tool names
(plans `type="tool", tool="scripting"` because module is called `scripting`) and
confuses task TYPE names with tool names (`type="tool", tool="exec"`).

**Design principle:** Don't add tool-specific deny rules ("there is NO X tool") — they
overfit and break when someone creates that tool. Instead, make the prompt structure
less ambiguous.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `kiso/brain.py` (module name references if any)

**Change:**

- [ ] Rename `<!-- MODULE: scripting -->` to `<!-- MODULE: code_execution -->` to avoid
      collision with potential tool names. Update `_load_modular_prompt` references.
      Content stays the same but opener clarifies: "Script execution via exec tasks:"
- [ ] Add one line to the core module after task type definitions:
      `type='tool' requires tool=<installed tool name>. Task type names (exec, search, etc.) are not tool names.`
- [ ] Update any briefer module references to "scripting" → "code_execution"
- [x] Unit tests pass (module rename is transparent)

---

### M715 — Planner: reinforce search-over-browser for research queries ✅

**Problem:** When browser tool is installed, the planner uses it for general web
research (navigate to Google, fill search form, read results) instead of the
built-in `search` task type. The browser subprocess stalls (CAPTCHA, slow pages,
no timeout) and the test times out at 300s.

The "Browser Availability" warning (brain.py line 1176) is only injected when
browser is NOT installed. When it IS installed, no warning exists — the planner
sees browser in the tool list and prefers it over search.

**Root cause:** The planner prompt module `web` (line 68) says "use built-in search
for research" but the `tools_rules` module (line 50) says "Listed tools are
confirmed installed — use directly." The planner resolves the conflict by choosing
browser because it's more "capable."

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Rewrite the `web` module rule (line 68) to clarify the three research paths:
      ```
      - **Research / information gathering:** use `search` task type (built-in,
        always available) or the `websearch` tool (if installed). NEVER use
        browser for web searches — no navigating to google.com, no filling
        search forms. Browser risks CAPTCHA blocks and is much slower.
      - **Browser is ONLY for:** navigating to a specific known URL the user
        gave you, and interacting with that specific page (click, fill, screenshot).
      ```
- [ ] Unit test: planner prompt contains "NEVER use browser for web searches"

---

### M717 — Fix briefer `replan` module hallucination ✅

**Problem:** The briefer LLM repeatedly hallucinate the module name `'replen'` instead
of `'replan'`. This wastes all 3 validation retries, forces a full-context fallback,
and adds ~30-50 s of overhead to the request (observed in F2 functional test timeout).

**Root cause:** The module description `"replan": "replan strategy, extend_replan"`
repeats the word "replan" three times on one line, creating token-level confusion
for the LLM.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Change:**

- [x] Rewrite the `replan` module description in `_BRIEFER_MODULE_DESCRIPTIONS` to
      avoid repeating the module name. New value:
      ```python
      "replan": "re-planning after failure, extend flag"
      ```
- [x] Unit test: verify `_BRIEFER_MODULE_DESCRIPTIONS["replan"]` does not contain
      the substring `"replan"` (the word should not appear in its own description). ✅

## Phase 39 — System package install & sudo awareness

> Root cause analysis from two real conversations where "puoi installare timg?" took
> 90+ seconds and 3 replan cycles, then "vai con sudo apt install timg" hit a
> CANNOT_TRANSLATE loop and failed completely.
>
> Five bugs, three in the prompt layer, two in sysenv.

### M731 — sysenv: detect distro and package manager ✅

**Problem:** `_collect_os_info()` returns only `platform.system()` / `.machine()` /
`.release()`. The planner sees `OS: Linux x86_64 (6.x.x)` but has no idea the
container runs Debian or that `apt` is the package manager. This forces unnecessary
web searches when the user asks to install a non-kiso system package.

**Files:** `kiso/sysenv.py`

**Change:**

- [x] In `_collect_os_info()`, add distro detection via `platform.freedesktop_os_release()`
      (Python 3.10+). Extract `PRETTY_NAME`, `ID`, and `ID_LIKE`. Wrap in try/except OSError
      for non-Linux hosts.
- [x] Add a `_detect_pkg_manager(distro_id, id_like)` helper: deterministic mapping
      (debian/ubuntu/linuxmint → apt, fedora/rhel/centos → dnf, alpine → apk).
      Return `None` if unknown.
- [x] In `build_system_env_section()`, append distro name to OS line:
      `OS: Linux x86_64 (6.x.x) — Debian GNU/Linux 12 (bookworm)`
      and add `Package manager: apt` line.
- [x] Unit test: `_collect_os_info()` returns `distro` key on Linux
- [x] Unit test: `_detect_pkg_manager("debian", "")` → `"apt"`
- [x] Unit test: `build_system_env_section` output contains "Package manager" line
      when distro is detected

---

### M732 — sysenv: detect current user and sudo availability ✅

**Problem:** The Docker container runs as root (no `USER` directive in Dockerfile).
`sudo` is not installed. Neither the planner nor the worker know this. When the user
says "sudo apt install timg", the worker generates `sudo apt install -y timg`, which
fails with `sudo: command not found`, triggers CANNOT_TRANSLATE, and loops 3 times.

**Files:** `kiso/sysenv.py`

**Change:**

- [x] In `collect_system_env()`, add `"user_info"` dict with `user`, `is_root`, `has_sudo`
- [x] `_collect_user_info()` helper: `pwd.getpwuid(os.getuid()).pw_name`, `os.getuid() == 0`,
      `shutil.which("sudo") is not None`
- [x] In `build_system_env_section()`, add line:
      `User: root (sudo not needed — already running as root)` or
      `User: kiso (sudo available)` / `User: kiso (sudo not available)`
- [x] Unit test: `collect_system_env` includes `user_info` with expected keys
- [x] Unit test: `_collect_user_info` root/non-root/sudo detection
- [x] Unit test: `build_system_env_section` shows correct user line for all 3 scenarios

---

### M733 — planner prompt: allow apt-get for user-requested system packages ✅

**Problem:** The `kiso_native` module (planner.md:29) says:
`Never apt-get/pip install directly — use uv pip install.`
This blanket ban prevents the planner from using apt-get even when the user explicitly
asks to install a system package that isn't a kiso tool.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`

**Change:**

- [x] Rewrite kiso_native module: split apt-get from pip, allow system packages
- [x] Keep tool_recovery module unchanged
- [x] Unit test: `kiso_native` module contains "system package manager"
- [x] Unit test: `tool_recovery` module still contains "Never apt-get/pip install to fix"
- [x] Existing test `test_planner_prompt_has_reinstall_guidance` still passes

---

### M734 — worker prompt: strip sudo when running as root ✅

**Files:** `kiso/roles/worker.md`

**Change:**

- [x] Replaced sudo rule with root-aware stripping instruction
- [x] Unit test: worker prompt contains "strip" and "sudo"
- [x] Unit test: worker prompt contains "CANNOT_TRANSLATE"

---

### M735 — exec handler: strip sudo from detail when running as root ✅

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Change:**

- [x] Chose simpler approach: strip in exec handler before translator call
- [x] In `_handle_exec_task`, after `get_system_env()`, check `user_info.is_root`
      and `detail.replace("sudo ", "")` if True
- [x] Unit test: "sudo apt-get install -y timg" → "apt-get install -y timg" when root
- [x] Unit test: "sudo apt-get install -y timg" → unchanged when not root
- [x] Unit test: detail without sudo unchanged regardless

## Phase 40 — External URL, network security & pub file access

> Root cause: pub file links returned to users (Discord, CLI) point to
> localhost:8333 which is unreachable from outside the Docker container.
> Additionally, the API is exposed on 0.0.0.0 without HTTPS by default.

### M736 — `external_url` setting + installer autodetect ✅

> **Deviation:** Post-deploy fix — IPv6 addresses need brackets in URLs.
> `curl -4` added to prefer IPv4. IPv6 fallback wraps in `http://[ip]:port`.
> Discovered during real VPS install (ifconfig.me returned IPv6).

**Problem:** `_report_pub_files()` uses FastAPI's `request.base_url` to build pub
URLs. Inside the container this is `http://localhost:8333`. Links like
`http://localhost:8333/pub/token/screenshot.png` are useless for remote users
and Discord.

**Files:** `install.sh`, `kiso/sysenv.py`, `kiso/worker/utils.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add `external_url` setting to config.toml template in `install.sh` (default: empty)
- [ ] In installer, after healthcheck and ports section:
      1. Autodetect public IP: `curl -sf https://ifconfig.me || curl -sf https://api.ipify.org`
      2. Pre-suggest: `External URL [http://{PUBLIC_IP}:{SERVER_PORT}]: `
      3. User can override with domain (`https://miobot.com`) or leave empty for local use
      4. Write to `config.toml` as `external_url = "..."`
- [ ] In `_report_pub_files()`: if `config.settings.get("external_url")` is set and non-empty,
      use it as prefix instead of `base_url` parameter
- [ ] Non-interactive mode: `--external-url <url>` flag, or autodetect if omitted
- [ ] Unit test: `_report_pub_files` uses `external_url` when configured
- [ ] Unit test: `_report_pub_files` falls back to `base_url` when `external_url` is empty

---

### M737 — Installer network access choice + HTTP warning ✅

**Problem:** The installer binds `0.0.0.0:8333` by default, exposing the API on
the public internet over HTTP. The CLI token is sent in plain text. While the
standard flow (docker exec) never sends the token over the network, the open port
is an unnecessary attack surface.

**Files:** `install.sh`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add network access prompt after ports section:
      ```
      Network access:
        1) Local only — API accessible only from this machine
        2) Public — API exposed to the network (token-protected)
      Choice [2]:
      ```
- [ ] Choice 1: `docker run -p "127.0.0.1:${SERVER_PORT}:8333" ...`
      Show info: "ℹ  Pub file links won't be reachable from outside.
      Set up a reverse proxy for external access. See: docs/https.md"
- [ ] Choice 2: `docker run -p "${SERVER_PORT}:8333" ...` (current behavior)
      Show warning: "⚠  API exposed over HTTP (no encryption).
      CLI token and API calls are visible to anyone on the network.
      For production use, set up HTTPS with a reverse proxy.
      See: docs/https.md"
- [ ] Store choice in `instances.json` as `"network": "local"|"public"` for
      update-instance mode to preserve the setting
- [ ] Non-interactive: `--network local|public` flag, default `public`
- [ ] Connector port range: same binding as main port (if local → local, if public → public)

---

### M738 — Messenger prompt: only use Published files URLs ✅

**Problem:** The messenger LLM hallucinated `sandbox:/mnt/data/screenshot.png`
(a ChatGPT code-interpreter URL format) instead of using the actual pub URL from
the task output's "Published files" section. Users receive broken, unreachable links.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/messenger.md`

**Change:**

- [ ] Add rule to messenger prompt:
      ```
      File links: when referencing files created by tasks, ONLY use URLs from the
      "Published files" section in task output. Never construct sandbox:, file://,
      or local filesystem paths as links. If no Published files URL exists, describe
      the file location as plain text without making it a link.
      ```
- [ ] Unit test: messenger prompt contains "Published files" rule

---

### M739 — HTTPS setup docs + docker-compose example ✅

**Problem:** No documentation exists for setting up HTTPS. Users on VPS need
guidance on securing their kiso instance.

**Files:** `docs/https.md` (new), `docker-compose.https.yml` (new)

**Change:**

- [ ] Create `docs/https.md` with four sections:
      - **Caddy** (recommended): docker-compose + Caddyfile, auto-HTTPS via Let's Encrypt.
        Prerequisites: domain pointing to VPS, ports 80/443 open.
      - **nginx**: example server block + certbot setup for Let's Encrypt
      - **Traefik**: docker-compose with labels, entrypoints, certificatesResolvers config
      - **SSH tunnel**: `ssh -L 8333:localhost:8333 vps` for quick dev access (no domain needed)
- [ ] Create `docker-compose.https.yml` with kiso + Caddy services:
      ```yaml
      services:
        kiso:
          image: kiso:latest
          # ... same as standalone, but NO ports exposed directly
          # Caddy handles external traffic
        caddy:
          image: caddy:2
          ports:
            - "80:80"
            - "443:443"
          volumes:
            - ./Caddyfile:/etc/caddy/Caddyfile
            - caddy_data:/data
      volumes:
        caddy_data:
      ```
- [x] Create `Caddyfile.example` (inline in docs/https.md)
- [x] Create `nginx.example.conf` (inline in docs/https.md)
- [x] Create `docker-compose.traefik.yml` (inline in docs/https.md)
- [x] Reference from installer HTTP warning message
- [x] Installer warning text: "See docs/https.md — we recommend Caddy + Let's Encrypt"

---

## Phase 43 — Unified conversation context for all LLM roles

> Root cause: classifier sees only "Last plan goal" but not kiso's response.
> When kiso asks "Vuoi che lo faccia?" and user replies "oh yeah", classifier
> doesn't know there was a pending question → classifies as "chat" instead of "plan".
>
> Broader issue: each role assembles conversation context independently with
> different helpers, different formats, and different levels of completeness.
> A unified helper would ensure consistency and prevent context gaps.

### M750 — `build_recent_context()` — unified conversation context helper ✅

**Problem:** Conversation context is assembled ad-hoc per role:
- Planner: `get_recent_messages()` → `_format_message_history()` → `[role] user: content`
- Classifier: only `Last plan goal: {goal}` — no conversation
- Messenger: `get_recent_messages()` but only if `include_recent=True` (default off)
- Inflight classifier: only plan goal — no conversation
- Reviewer/worker/curator/searcher: no conversation context (acceptable for their scope)

Each role that needs conversation context uses different code paths, different
limits, and different formatting. This caused the "oh yeah" bug where the
classifier couldn't tell the user was confirming kiso's install proposal.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/store.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Create `build_recent_context(messages: list[dict], *, max_chars: int = 500) -> str`
      helper in brain.py. Takes the raw message list from `get_recent_messages()` and
      produces a compact conversation summary:
      ```
      [user] root: vai su guidance.studio poi fai uno screenshot
      [kiso] Per navigare serve il browser tool. Vuoi che lo installi?
      [user] root: oh yeah
      ```
      Format: `[user] {username}: {content}` for user messages,
      `[kiso] {content[:200]}` for assistant/system messages (truncated — kiso
      responses can be long).
- [ ] `max_chars` budget truncates from the oldest messages first (keep most
      recent turns intact).
- [ ] Reuse `_format_message_history()` internally or replace it — one function
      for all roles.
- [ ] Unit test: builds correct format with mixed user/assistant messages
- [ ] Unit test: truncation keeps most recent messages
- [ ] Unit test: empty list → empty string

---

### M751 — Classifier uses conversation context ✅

**Problem:** Classifier receives only `Last plan goal` but not kiso's last
response. When kiso asks a yes/no question and the user confirms with a short
reply ("oh yeah", "sì", "vai", "ok"), the classifier misclassifies as "chat".

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] In `_process_message` (loop.py), fetch last 2-3 messages via
      `get_recent_messages(db, session, limit=3)` and pass them to the classifier
      via `build_recent_context(messages)`
- [ ] Update `build_classifier_messages` to accept and inject conversation context
      instead of just plan goal. Format:
      ```
      ## Recent Conversation
      [user] root: vai su guidance.studio e fai screenshot
      [kiso] Serve il browser tool. Vuoi che lo installi?

      ## New Message
      oh yeah
      ```
- [ ] Update classifier prompt to mention: "If Recent Conversation shows kiso asked
      a yes/no question and the new message is a short affirmative → plan."
- [ ] Unit test: "oh yeah" after install proposal → classified as "plan"
- [ ] Unit test: "oh yeah" with no context → classified as "chat"
- [ ] Live test: same scenarios with real LLM

---

### M752 — Inflight classifier uses conversation context ✅

**Problem:** Same as M751 but for the inflight classifier — it only sees plan goal,
not kiso's messages. A mid-plan "sì" could be misclassified.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Update `build_inflight_classifier_messages` to accept recent conversation context
- [ ] Pass last 2 messages from session when building inflight classifier input
- [ ] Unit test: inflight classifier with conversation context parses correctly

---

### M753 — Messenger always sees recent conversation ✅

**Problem:** `include_recent` defaults to False in most messenger calls. When the
messenger doesn't see the conversation history, it lacks context for coherent
multi-turn responses.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Evaluate which messenger call sites should have `include_recent=True`:
      - Fast-path chat: already True? If not, enable
      - Plan msg tasks: should see at least last 2-3 turns for coherence
      - Error/cancel messages: low priority, can stay without
- [ ] If enabling broadly: use `build_recent_context()` with a small budget
      (300-500 chars) to keep token cost low
- [ ] Unit test: messenger messages include Recent Conversation section when enabled

---

### M754 — Planner migrates to `build_recent_context()` ✅

**Problem:** Planner uses its own `_format_message_history()` to format recent
messages. This is the same logic that `build_recent_context()` (M750) will
provide. Having two code paths for the same thing creates drift risk.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Change:**

- [ ] Replace `_format_message_history(recent)` call in `_gather_planner_context()`
      with `build_recent_context(recent)` (same output format, single source of truth)
- [ ] If `_format_message_history` has no other callers, remove it
- [ ] If summarizer also uses it, migrate summarizer too
- [ ] Unit test: planner messages still contain `[user]` and `[kiso]` conversation lines
- [ ] Regression test: existing planner message tests still pass

---

## Phase 45 — Document reader tool

> NOTE: This is an external tool repo (`kiso-run/tool-docreader`), not core code.
> Only the registry.json update is done in this repo.

### M761 — Tool: `docreader` — PDF/DOCX/CSV text extraction (registry only) ✅

**Problem:** Users need to process uploaded documents (PDFs, DOCX, XLSX, CSV).
Today kiso can do `exec python3 script.py` with libraries, but the planner must
invent the script, install deps, handle errors — fragile and slow.

A dedicated tool with a clean args schema makes this reliable and one-step.

**Files:** new tool repo `kiso-run/tool-docreader` (external), + `registry.json` update

**Scope:**

```
Actions (via args.action):
  - read(file, pages?)     → extracted text
  - search(file, query)    → matching passages with page/line numbers

Supported formats: PDF (pdfplumber), DOCX (python-docx), CSV/XLSX (pandas),
                   TXT/MD (direct read)

Input: file path relative to workspace (uploads/ or session dir)
Output: extracted text on stdout
```

**Change (in core repo):**

- [ ] Add `docreader` to `registry.json`

**Change (in tool-docreader repo — separate):**

- [ ] Create tool repo structure: kiso.toml, pyproject.toml, run.py
- [ ] Implement read action: detect format by extension, extract text
- [ ] Implement search action: extract text, find matching passages
- [ ] Unit tests in tool repo

---

## Phase 46 — Skill system documentation

### M762 — Document MD skills: scope, limitations, and when to use them ✅

**Problem:** The MD skill system exists but has no documentation explaining what it
does, what it doesn't do, and when it's appropriate. Without this, users (and future
developers) will create skills for things they can't influence (content quality,
tool behavior) and be disappointed.

**Files:** `docs/skills.md` (new or update `docs/skill-development.md`)

**Change:**

- [ ] Document the skill pipeline clearly:
      1. `.md` files in `~/.kiso/skills/` with YAML frontmatter (name, summary)
      2. `discover_md_skills()` scans the directory (cached 30s)
      3. Briefer decides which skills are relevant for the current request
      4. Selected skill instructions are injected into the **planner prompt only**
      5. The planner reads them and incorporates them into plan structure/strategy
- [ ] Document what skills CAN influence:
      - Plan structure: which task types, in what order
      - Strategy: how many sources to check, whether to verify before reporting
      - Tool selection: prefer tool X over exec for this type of task
      - Task detail wording: more specific exec descriptions
- [ ] Document what skills CANNOT influence:
      - Content generated by the worker (shell commands, script content)
      - Tool behavior (aider review quality, browser actions)
      - Messenger response style (has its own prompt, doesn't see skills)
      - Code quality in generated scripts
- [ ] Explain: skills shape the PLAN, not the EXECUTION
- [ ] Add examples: good skill (workflow guidance) vs bad skill (content instructions)
- [ ] Reference from README and `kiso skill --help` output

---

## Phase 47 — Messenger URL Hallucination Fix

**Problem:** The messenger hallucinates URLs when the planner doesn't include actual URLs in the msg task detail. Observed: browser tool output contained `http://77.42.46.159:8333/pub/4ab9292c8b224bb9/screenshot.png`, reviewer learning captured it correctly, but the messenger invented `https://kiso.run/attachment/guidance_studio_screenshot.png` because the planner wrote a vague detail like "il file è stato salvato nella workspace".

**Root cause:** `_format_plan_outputs_for_msg` feeds plan outputs to the planner for msg detail generation, but there's no mechanism ensuring published file URLs survive into the msg task detail. The planner paraphrases instead of preserving verbatim URLs.

### M763 — Inject published file URLs into msg task detail ✅
- [x] In `_format_plan_outputs_for_msg` (worker/utils.py), extract lines matching `Published files:` and the URL lines that follow from plan outputs via `_extract_published_urls()`
- [x] Collect all published file URLs into a dedicated `## Published Files` section at the top of the formatted output, so they are prominent and not buried/truncated
- [x] Shared `_PUB_FILES_MARKER` constant ties writer (`_format_pub_note`) and reader (`_extract_published_urls`)
- [x] Add test: plan outputs with published file URLs → formatted output preserves them in dedicated section

### M764 — ~~Planner prompt: verbatim URL rule for msg tasks~~ SKIPPED
- Reverted: unnecessary with M763 in place — the messenger already receives exact URLs via the `## Published Files` section. Adding planner prompt rules would cause overfitting.

### M765 — Messenger prompt: reinforce Published Files section awareness ✅
- [x] Messenger prompt: reference the `## Published Files` section by name so the LLM knows where to find exact URLs
- [x] Simplified wording: "ONLY use exact URLs from ## Published Files or Published files: lines. Never construct, shorten, or guess URLs."
- [x] Add test: messenger prompt mentions Published Files section

---

## Phase 48 — Cancel Kills Running Job

**Problem:** When the user sends Ctrl+C (or cancel via REST/stop-message), the `cancel_event` is set but only checked at batch boundaries in `_execute_plan`. The currently running subprocess (`_run_subprocess` → `proc.communicate()`) keeps running until it finishes naturally. This means long-running exec/tool tasks can't be interrupted.

### M766 — Pass cancel_event to _run_subprocess ✅
- [x] Add `cancel_event: asyncio.Event | None = None` parameter to `_run_subprocess` in `worker/utils.py`
- [x] When `cancel_event` is provided, race `proc.communicate()` vs `cancel_event.wait()` via `asyncio.wait(FIRST_COMPLETED)`; if cancel fires first, `_kill_proc()` sends SIGTERM, waits 2s grace, then SIGKILL
- [x] Handle already-set cancel_event: kill immediately after process creation
- [x] Return `("", "cancelled", False, -15)` on cancel
- [x] Unit tests: cancel kills subprocess, normal completion unaffected, no cancel_event unchanged, already-set cancel

### M767 — Thread cancel_event through exec and tool handlers ✅
- [x] Add `cancel_event` to `_PlanCtx` dataclass; set from `_execute_plan`'s `cancel_event` param
- [x] Pass `ctx.cancel_event` through `_handle_exec_task` → `_exec_task` → `_run_subprocess`
- [x] Pass `ctx.cancel_event` through `_handle_tool_task` → `_tool_task` → `_run_subprocess`
- [x] When `_run_subprocess` returns `exit_code==-15, stderr=="cancelled"`, mark task as `"cancelled"` and return `stop_replan=True, replan_reason="cancelled"` — skips review
- [x] Integration tests: cancel during exec task kills subprocess + normal completion with cancel_event unset

### M768 — Cancel check after in-flight task completes ✅
- [x] Add cancel check after each sequential task completes (inside batch loop, after handler return)
- [x] Add cancel check after parallel batch completes (after gather returns)
- [x] Both paths cancel remaining tasks and return `"cancelled"` replan_reason
- [x] Test: cancel during task → cancel_event is set, remaining tasks would be skipped

---

## Phase 49 — Pub URL Port Mismatch (deploy bug)

**Problem:** The browser tool publishes files with port 8333 (the manager container `kiso`), but the actual kiso instance serving `/pub/` routes runs on port 8334 (`kiso-kiso`). Result: published URLs return 404 from the wrong container.

### M769 — Pub URL uses instance port, not manager port ✅
- [x] Root cause: `ask_network_and_external_url` runs before port assignment, uses default 8333; if actual SERVER_PORT differs, external_url has wrong port
- [x] Fix: after port assignment in install.sh, correct EXTERNAL_URL if it ends with `:8333` and SERVER_PORT differs
- [x] The `_report_pub_files` code (M736) already prefers `external_url` over request-derived base_url — the fix is purely in the installer
- [x] Tests: port updated when different, unchanged when matching, empty unaffected, fix block present in install.sh
- **Note:** existing installations need manual fix: `kiso env set external_url http://IP:ACTUAL_PORT`

Simplified: code-level context injection only, no prompt rule.

- [ ] If docreader IS installed, no note needed — briefer will select it naturally
- [ ] Add test: planner context includes upload note only when docreader missing
