### M870 — Post-preset workflow tests (tools pre-installed) ✅

**Problem:** F17 mixes two concerns: testing the install flow (fragile, LLM
flakiness on approval cycle) and testing multi-tool orchestration (the real
value). By separating them, we get:
- Install flow: tested by F1/F1a (already works)
- Tool usage workflows: tested with tools pre-installed (no install overhead)

**Approach:** New file `tests/functional/test_preset_workflows.py` with a
session-scoped fixture that installs the default preset (browser, ocr, aider)
once. All tests in the file use the pre-installed tools directly.

Marked `@pytest.mark.extended` because the initial preset install is slow
(~5 min for browser+ocr+aider deps). Individual tests are fast (~1-2 min
each) since tools are already available.

**Fixture: `preset_installed` (session-scoped)**
- Runs `kiso preset install default` inside the Docker container
- Invalidates tool cache so `discover_tools()` sees new tools
- Verifies browser, ocr, aider are all discoverable
- Yields → tests run → no cleanup needed (temp dir)

**Tests:**

**F27 — Browse and describe a website**
- Request: `"vai su example.com e dimmi cosa c'è scritto"`
- Assert: success, Italian response, mentions "example" or "domain"
- Validates: browser tool works end-to-end without install flow

**F28 — Screenshot + OCR text extraction**
- Request: `"fai uno screenshot di example.com ed estrai il testo"`
- Assert: success, .png published, output mentions "example"
- Validates: browser→ocr pipeline, cross-tool file routing (M826)

**F29 — Write code with aider**
- Request: `"usa aider per scrivere uno script hello.py che stampa 'ciao'"`
- Assert: success, aider tool task used, hello.py in session workspace
- Validates: aider tool works, file creation via tool

**F30 — Full pipeline: browse → OCR → code → exec → msg**
- Plan 1: `"fai screenshot di example.com e estrai il testo con OCR"`
  - Assert: screenshot + OCR text
- Plan 2: `"usa aider per scrivere uno script che conta le parole nel testo
  estratto, eseguilo e dimmi il risultato"`
  - Assert: aider used, exec ran script, output has word counts
- This replaces F17 — same coverage but no install flow fragility

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_preset_workflows.py`,
`tests/functional/conftest.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add `preset_installed` session-scoped fixture in conftest or in the
  new file. Installs default preset via `kiso preset install default`
  subprocess call
- [ ] Create `tests/functional/test_preset_workflows.py` with F27-F30
- [ ] Mark all tests `@pytest.mark.extended` (slow fixture)
- [ ] F30 is 2-plan — uses same `run_message` pattern as F24-F26
- [ ] Consider deprecating/removing F17 once F30 is stable
- [ ] Update tests/README.md with preset workflow test description

### M871 — Exec translator: fallback when detail specifies unavailable tool ✅

**Problem (kiso behavior):** The planner writes "Check if port 9090 is
listening using the ss command" — specifying HOW instead of WHAT. The exec
translator tries ss, it's not available → CANNOT_TRANSLATE → replan loop.
The planner prompt says "detail: WHAT, not HOW" but the LLM doesn't always
follow it.

This is a general problem: any exec detail that hardcodes a specific tool
is fragile across environments. The translator should be resilient.

**Fix:** Add a fallback rule to the worker prompt (exec translator): "If
the task detail specifies a command/tool not in available binaries, ignore
the specific tool and accomplish the goal using available alternatives."
This makes the translator robust to overly-specific planner details.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/worker.md`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add fallback rule to worker.md exec translator prompt
- [ ] Unit test: translator prompt contains the fallback rule
- [x] Verify prompt size stays within limits

---

### M872 — Messenger: synthesize foreign-language content in response language ✅

**Problem (kiso behavior):** The messenger receives "Answer in Italian" +
browser output in English. It copies the English content verbatim instead
of summarizing in Italian. Result: mixed-language response that looks
English-dominant.

The messenger prompt says "Synthesize task outputs" but doesn't say
"translate content in a different language to the response language."

**Fix:** Add to messenger prompt: "When task outputs contain content in a
different language than your response language, summarize the relevant
parts in the response language — do not copy foreign-language text verbatim."

**Files:** `kiso/roles/messenger.md`, `tests/test_prompts.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add language synthesis rule to messenger.md
- [x] Verify prompt size stays within limits

### M876 — Fix F17: planner confuses "kiso" CLI with tool name ✅

**Problem:** When the planner generates a tool task for an uninstalled tool,
the validation feedback says:
```
plan an exec task: `kiso tool install aider`, then replan
```
The LLM parses the backticked text and extracts "kiso" as a tool name,
generating `type="tool", tool="kiso"`. This cascades into more validation
errors until retries are exhausted.

**Root cause:** Two issues:
1. The planner has no concept of "kiso is a CLI binary, not a tool." When it
   sees `kiso tool install`, it doesn't know `kiso` is the command and
   `tool install` is a subcommand.
2. Backtick formatting in validation feedback looks like tool name references
   to the LLM. The LLM treats backticked text as identifiers.

**Fix (three changes):**

1. **Core prompt disambiguation** — add one line to planner.md core:
   `"kiso is the system CLI (not a tool). Use it only in exec task details."`
   This permanently disambiguates kiso from tool names.

2. **Remove backticks from validation feedback** — the install-approved
   error at brain.py ~line 724 and the needs_install conflict at ~line 924
   currently use backticks around `kiso tool install`. Replace with natural
   language: "plan an exec task to install {name} via kiso CLI, then replan."

3. **Remove backticks from Install Status context** — brain.py ~line 1349
   currently says "plan exec `kiso tool install {name}`". Replace with:
   "plan an exec task to install {name} using the kiso CLI, then replan."

The principle: validation feedback and context injections should use natural
language, not code formatting. The exec translator converts natural language
to commands — the planner doesn't need to see the exact command.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add "kiso is the system CLI (not a tool)" to core prompt
- [ ] Remove backticks from validation feedback (install-approved error)
- [ ] Remove backticks from Install Status context injection
- [ ] Remove backticks from needs_install + tool task conflict feedback
- [ ] Update unit tests that check these error messages
- [x] Verify prompt size within limits
- [ ] Verify M862 registry validation still works (uses _INSTALL_NAME_RE)

---

### M874 — Fix "Four" test: ask for numeral explicitly ✅

**Problem:** `test_plan_then_msg_execution` asserts `"4" in text` but the
LLM returned "Four." The test asks "What is 2+2?" without specifying the
format. The messenger has no reason to prefer digits over words.

**Fix:** Change the test question to explicitly request a numeral:
"What is 2 + 2? Reply with the numeral only." Then `assert "4" in text`
is correct — the test is specific about what it expects.

**Files:** `tests/live/test_flows.py`

**Tasks:**

- [ ] Keep assertion `"4" in text`

### M875 — Test assertion normalization for Latin-alphabet output ✅

**Problem:** Assertions on LLM output are fragile to format variations:
accents (París/paris), case, number words (Four/4). We've fixed these
case-by-case. A general helper reduces future fragility.

**Approach:** `_normalize_for_assertion(text, latin=True)` helper:
- `latin=True` (default): strip accents (NFKD), lowercase
- `latin=False`: lowercase only (no accent stripping — destructive for
  Cyrillic/CJK)

Default True because most tests use Latin-alphabet languages (IT/EN/ES).
Non-Latin tests (Russian, Chinese) pass `latin=False`.

**New tests for non-Latin scripts:**

**F31 — Russian response quality**
- Request: `"Какие 3 самых популярных языка программирования?"`
- Assert: success, Russian function words in output, mentions programming
  languages, `latin=False` for normalization

**F32 — Chinese response quality**
- Request: `"最受欢迎的3种编程语言是什么？简要说明"`
- Assert: success, Chinese characters in output, mentions programming
  languages, `latin=False` for normalization

**Language helpers update:** Add `_RU_WORDS` and `_ZH_INDICATOR` to
`assert_language`. Russian uses function words like Latin languages.
Chinese doesn't have function words — detect by character range (CJK
Unified Ideographs U+4E00-U+9FFF).

**Files:** `tests/functional/conftest.py`, `tests/functional/test_core_flows.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add `_normalize_for_assertion(text, latin=True)` helper in conftest
- [ ] Refactor `_strip_accents` in test_roles.py to use the shared helper
- [ ] Add `_RU_WORDS` and Russian support to `assert_language`
- [ ] Add Chinese detection (CJK character range) to `assert_language`
- [ ] F31: Russian Q&A test with `latin=False`
- [ ] F32: Chinese Q&A test with `latin=False`
- [ ] Update existing accent-sensitive assertions to use the helper

## Phase 61 — Multilingual support + tool cache reliability

### M877 — Classifier: support non-Latin language detection ✅

**Problem (kiso behavior):** The classifier returns "plan:en" for Russian
and Chinese messages. The user writes in Cyrillic/CJK but gets an English
response. Root cause: the classifier prompt has zero non-Latin examples and
says "Default to 'en' when uncertain."

The model (gemini-2.5-flash-lite) CAN detect Russian and Chinese — it just
isn't given confidence to do so because the prompt only shows IT/EN/ES/FR
examples.

**Principle:** A generalista bot must detect the user's language regardless
of script. The fix is in the prompt (add diverse examples), not in the model
or in code. The "default to en" rule stays for genuinely ambiguous cases,
but the prompt should make non-Latin scripts non-ambiguous.

**Fix:** Add 2-3 non-Latin examples to the classifier prompt:
- `"plan:ru"` for Cyrillic
- `"plan:zh"` for CJK
- `"chat:ar"` for Arabic (optional, shows the model the pattern)

Also change "Default to 'en' when uncertain" to "Default to 'en' only when
the script is ambiguous. Cyrillic → likely ru/uk/bg, CJK → likely zh/ja/ko,
Arabic script → likely ar/fa." This gives the model a decision tree for
non-Latin scripts without hardcoding specific languages.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/classifier.md`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add non-Latin examples to classifier.md (ru, zh, optionally ar)
- [ ] Refine "default to en" rule: only for genuinely ambiguous script
- [ ] Unit test: classifier prompt contains "ru" and "zh" examples
- [ ] Verify F31/F32 functional tests collect correctly (already written)

---

### M878 — Invalidate tools cache before replan planner call ✅

**Problem (kiso behavior):** When a plan installs a tool and then replans,
the replan's `run_planner()` call hits the 30-second TTL cache in
`discover_tools()` and sees the OLD tool list. The planner doesn't know the
tool was just installed → generates exec tasks instead of tool tasks.

This is the core reason F17 fails: after installing OCR, the replan planner
still sees the old list without OCR → generates `exec: Run Tesseract OCR`
instead of `type="tool", tool="ocr"`. Same for aider.

**Evidence:** In `_execute_plan()` (loop.py:1641/1692), the cache IS
refreshed after each task execution. But in the replan loop (loop.py:2343),
`run_planner()` is called WITHOUT invalidating the cache first.

**Principle:** Every planning decision must see the current state. The TTL
cache is fine for performance within a single plan execution (tasks happen
fast). But between plans (replan, new message), the state may have changed
(tools installed, config reloaded). Cache must be invalidated at plan
boundaries.

**Fix:** Call `invalidate_tools_cache()` before `run_planner()` in:
1. The replan loop (loop.py ~line 2340)
2. The initial planner call (loop.py ~line 2560) — already fresh, but
   explicit invalidation prevents future bugs

This is one line of code. The impact is: every planner call sees fresh tool
state. The TTL cache still helps within `_execute_plan` (multiple
discover_tools calls in the same plan execution stay cached).

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add `invalidate_tools_cache()` before `run_planner()` in replan loop
- [ ] Add `invalidate_tools_cache()` before initial `run_planner()` call
- [ ] Unit test: verify that replan path invalidates cache
- [ ] Consider: should `run_planner` always invalidate at the start?
  (brain.py ~line 1123) — probably yes, as a safety net

---

## Phase 62 — Language fallback + install context compression

### M879 — Rewrite M877: classifier language fallback without script mapping ✅

**Problem:** M877 added "Cyrillic → ru" to the classifier prompt. This is
wrong — Cyrillic is used by Russian, Ukrainian, Bulgarian, Serbian, etc.
CJK is used by Chinese, Japanese, Korean. You can't map script to language.

The REAL bug is in brain.py: when the classifier LLM returns a bare category
without a language code (e.g., "chat" instead of "chat:ru"), the code
defaults to "en":
```python
if result in CLASSIFIER_CATEGORIES:
    return result, "en"  # ← forces English for ALL undetected languages
```

**Fix (two changes):**

1. **Revert M877's prompt change** — remove "Cyrillic → ru, CJK → zh" from
   classifier.md. Instead, strengthen the format instruction: "ALWAYS include
   the language code. Never return a bare category without :xx."

2. **Code fallback** — when the classifier returns a bare category (no colon),
   return the category with **empty string** as language instead of "en".
   In the planner/messenger flow, empty language means "no language detected"
   → no "Answer in {lang}." prefix → the messenger detects language from the
   user's message text (it already has this rule: "If absent, match the most
   recent user message language").

This is generalizable:
- Works for ALL languages (no script mapping)
- No hardcoded language assumptions
- The messenger's own language detection is the safety net
- Zero overfitting

**Files:** `kiso/roles/classifier.md`, `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`,
`tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Revert classifier.md: remove "Cyrillic → ru, CJK → zh, Arabic → ar"
  mapping. Replace with: "ALWAYS include the language code after the colon.
  Detect the actual language — do not default to en for non-Latin scripts."
- [ ] In brain.py `classify_message()`: change bare-category fallback from
  `return result, "en"` to `return result, ""`
- [ ] In loop.py: when `user_lang` is empty, skip the "Answer in {lang}."
  prefix. The messenger will detect language from the user message.
- [ ] Unit test: bare category "chat" → returns ("chat", "")
- [ ] Unit test: formatted "chat:ru" → returns ("chat", "ru") (unchanged)
- [ ] Unit test: empty lang → no "Answer in" prefix injected

---

### M880 — Compress install turns in replan context ✅

**Problem:** After the install-approve-install cycle (3-5 messages), the
planner's recent message context is full of install noise. When the planner
finally needs to USE the tool, it's confused by the install history and
generates exec tasks instead of tool tasks.

This is why F17 fails: after 3 install cycles (browser, ocr, aider), the
context has 15+ install-related messages. The planner can't distinguish
between "install this tool" and "use this tool" because both are in
recent history.

F30 passes because tools are pre-installed — zero install noise in context.

**Fix: structured compression of install turns.**

In `build_recent_context()` or in the planner message building, detect
consecutive install-related messages (propose → approve → install result)
and compress them into a single structured line:

Before (5 messages):
```
[user] Use aider to write word_count.py
[kiso] Vuoi installare aider?
[user] sì, installa il tool aider
[kiso] Tool aider installato. Replan...
[user] Use aider to write word_count.py  ← repeated by helper
```

After (2 lines):
```
[install completed] aider is now available.
[user] Use aider to write word_count.py
```

**Implementation approach:**

In `build_recent_context()` (worker/utils.py), add a compression pass:
1. Scan messages for install patterns (kiso msg with "install" keywords +
   user reply with approval keywords + kiso msg with install result)
2. Replace the group with a single "[install completed] {tool} available."
   line + keep the original user request
3. Non-install messages pass through unchanged

This is deterministic (pattern matching on message content), generalizable
(works for any tool install, not just F17), and doesn't depend on LLM.

**Alternative considered:** Have the briefer filter install messages. Rejected
because the briefer is an LLM call (adds latency + flakiness) and we need
deterministic behavior here.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/utils.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Add `_compress_install_turns(messages)` function in worker/utils.py
- [ ] Detect install proposal (kiso msg with install/needs_install keywords)
  + approval (user msg with affirmative) + result (kiso msg with installed)
- [ ] Replace group with single "[install completed] {tool}" line
- [ ] Keep original user request that triggered the install proposal
- [ ] Call from `build_recent_context()` before formatting
- [ ] Unit test: install sequence → compressed to 2 lines
- [ ] Unit test: non-install messages → unchanged
- [ ] Unit test: mixed install + regular messages → only install compressed

---

`assert_language(text, lang)` that compares the target language's score against
the highest non-target score. `assert_italian` becomes
`assert_language(text, "it")`.

### M838 — F21: Replan recovery after exec failure ✅

**Scenario:** User asks to read a file that doesn't exist. Exec fails →
reviewer triggers replan → planner recovers by explaining the error to the user.

**File:** `tests/functional/test_core_flows.py`

**Test: `test_replan_recovery_missing_file`**
- Request: `"leggi il file /tmp/file_inesistente_kiso_test_xyz99.txt e dimmi cosa contiene"`
- Assert:
  - Pipeline completes (no exception, no timeout)
  - `len(result.plans) >= 1` (at least one plan attempted)
  - `result.last_plan_msg_output` is non-empty (user got a response)
  - Output mentions the problem: any of "non esiste", "non trovato",
    "not found", "errore", "impossibile", "non è stato possibile",
    "inesistente" (case-insensitive)
  - Note: `result.success` may be True or False — both are acceptable.
    The key is graceful handling, not a specific outcome.

**Why this matters:** Replan is one of the most common production flows.
When exec fails, the system must not crash, loop forever, or silently drop
the user's request. It must communicate the problem.

**Tasks:**
- [x] Implement `TestF21ReplanRecovery::test_replan_recovery_missing_file`

### M839 — F22: Nonexistent tool request ✅

    "non è disponibile", "non trovato", "not available", "not found"

**Why this matters:** Validates M831 (registry_hints as decision criterion) and

### M840 — F23: Cross-session knowledge sharing ✅

**Scenario:** Teach a fact in session A, then query it from session B. Validates
the curator pipeline promotes learnings to global facts that are retrievable
across sessions.

**File:** `tests/functional/test_core_flows.py`

**Test: `test_cross_session_knowledge_sharing`**
- Session A: `"ricordati che il progetto Artemis usa PostgreSQL 16 come database principale"`
- Wait for background knowledge task (curator promote)
- Switch to session B (new session, same DB)
- Session B: `"che database usa il progetto Artemis?"`
- Assert:
  - Session A: success (fact taught)
  - Session B: success
  - Session B output mentions "postgresql" or "postgres" (fact was recalled)
  - Italian response in both

**Implementation note:** The `run_message` fixture is per-session. To test
cross-session, we need either:
(a) A second `run_message` instance with a different `func_session`, or
(b) Manually call `_process_message` with a different session after teaching.
Option (a) is cleaner — create a `run_message_b` fixture or parametrize.
Simplest: after the first `run_message` call, manually create a second session
in the same DB and call `_process_message` directly.

**Tasks:**
- [x] Implement `TestF23CrossSessionKnowledge::test_cross_session_knowledge_sharing`
- [x] Use same `func_db` but different session name for session B
- [x] Ensure background knowledge task completes before querying session B

## Phase 63 — Eliminate l10n layer, classifier returns language name

**Problem:** The language handling pipeline has an unnecessary mapping layer.
The classifier returns ISO 639-1 codes (e.g. `"ru"`, `"zh"`), then `_msg_task`
maps them to English names via `LANG_NAMES` dict to build "Answer in {lang}."
prefix. But `LANG_NAMES` only covers 6 languages — Russian, Chinese, Japanese,
Korean, Arabic, etc. all fall back to "English", causing the messenger to
respond in English instead of the detected language. This is the root cause of
F32 (Chinese response in English).

Additionally, `detect_user_lang()` duplicates language detection with a
keyword heuristic (only 5 languages), and `REPLAN_TEMPLATES` provides
localized replan notifications for only 5 languages. Both are redundant: the
classifier already detected the language, and for unsupported languages
everything falls back to English anyway.

**Solution:** Eliminate the entire l10n layer:
1. Classifier returns full language name (e.g. `plan:Russian`, `chat_kb:Chinese`)
2. `_msg_task` uses `response_lang` directly — no mapping
3. Replan notifications use English only (system messages, user understands)
4. Delete `l10n.py`, `detect_user_lang`, `LANG_NAMES`, `LANG_MARKERS`,
   `REPLAN_TEMPLATES`

---

### M881 — Classifier returns full language name ✅

**Problem:** Classifier returns ISO 639-1 codes. `_msg_task` needs English
language names. The mapping dict (`LANG_NAMES`) only covers 6 languages,
silently falling back to "English" for everything else.

**Approach:** Change the classifier prompt to return full language names
directly (e.g. `plan:Russian`). Update `classify_message()` parsing to accept
any non-empty string after `:` (not just 2-char codes). This eliminates the
need for any language name mapping.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/classifier.md`, `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Update `classifier.md`: change format from `plan:xx` (ISO 639-1) to
  `plan:LanguageName` (e.g. `plan:Russian`, `chat_kb:Chinese`, `chat:English`)
- [x] Update examples in prompt accordingly
- [x] Update `classify_message()` parsing: remove `len(lang) == 2` check,
  accept any non-empty stripped string after `:`
- [x] Update docstring: `lang` is now a language name, not ISO code
- [x] Update defensive "category:xx" parsing for new format
- [x] Unit test: classifier parsing accepts `"plan:Russian"`, `"chat:Chinese"`,
  `"chat_kb:English"`
- [x] Unit test: fallback for bare category (`"plan"`) still returns empty lang

---

### M882 — _msg_task uses language name directly, remove LANG_NAMES ✅

**Problem:** `_msg_task` maps ISO codes to names via `LANG_NAMES`. After M881,
`response_lang` already contains the full name.

**Approach:** Use `response_lang` directly in the "Answer in {lang}." prefix.
Remove `LANG_NAMES` dict and its import.

- [x] Remove `LANG_NAMES` dict from l10n.py
- [x] Update 3 response_lang tests: change `response_lang="it"` to
  `response_lang="Italian"`, update assertions accordingly
- [x] Verify `_ANSWER_IN_RE` in `_maybe_inject_intent_msg` still works
  (it matches `"Answer in \w[\w\s]*\."` — language names fit this pattern)

### M885 — Flatten OutputBudgets class into module constants ✅

**Problem:** `OutputBudgets` class in `kiso/worker/utils.py` defines 7
constants, then 5 of them are immediately re-aliased to module-level names:

```python
class OutputBudgets:
    REPLAN_EXEC = 1000
    ...
_REPLAN_OUTPUT_LIMIT = OutputBudgets.REPLAN_EXEC  # duplicate name
```

Two names for the same values. The class adds no grouping value since most
code uses the module-level aliases anyway. The remaining 2 constants
(`PLAN_OUTPUTS`, `PUB_SCAN_MAX`) are used directly via `OutputBudgets.X` in
only 3 places. No tests import `OutputBudgets`.

**Approach:** Delete the class. Keep the module-level constants (already the
primary usage). Add `_PLAN_OUTPUTS_BUDGET` and `_PUB_SCAN_MAX` as new
module constants for the 2 that were class-only. Update the 3 call sites.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/utils.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Replace `class OutputBudgets` with flat module-level constants
- [x] Add `_PUB_SCAN_MAX = 1000` (was `OutputBudgets.PUB_SCAN_MAX`)
- [x] Replace `OutputBudgets.PLAN_OUTPUTS` default in
  `_format_plan_outputs_for_msg` with `_PLAN_OUTPUTS_BUDGET`
- [x] Replace `OutputBudgets.PUB_SCAN_MAX` (2 uses in `_report_pub_files`)
  with `_PUB_SCAN_MAX`
- [x] Remove duplicate aliases (the module constants ARE the values now)
- [x] Verify no tests or external code import `OutputBudgets`

---

### M886 — Test runner: compact failure summary for LLM paste ✅

**Problem:** When tests fail, `run_tests.sh` says "Some suites failed —
check output above." and you have to scroll through hundreds of lines of
passing tests, Docker build output, and pytest boilerplate to find the
failures. Pasting the full output into an LLM wastes context on noise.

**Goal:** At the end of a run with failures, print a compact debug block
that contains ONLY:
1. One-line-per-failure summary (test name + short error)
2. For each failure: assertion error + captured log (classifier output,
   LLM calls, briefer decisions — the INFO lines that matter)
3. No passing tests, no Docker build output, no traceback frames from
   stdlib/dependencies (only the final assertion + app frames)

The block should be copy-pasteable as-is into an LLM context.

**Approach:** Capture pytest stdout/stderr to a temp file via `tee` while
still showing output live. On failure, parse the captured output:

1. Extract the `=== FAILURES ===` section (pytest groups each failure with
   its captured log/stderr)
2. For each failure block:
   - Extract test name from the `___ TestName ___` header
   - Extract the assertion line (last `E   ...` lines or `AssertionError`)
   - Extract `Captured log call` section (contains classifier, briefer,
     planner INFO lines — the actual debug data)
   - Extract `Captured stderr call` section (contains same INFO lines
     when running in Docker)
   - Skip stdlib traceback frames (only keep frames from `kiso/` or
     `tests/`)
3. Compress: truncate captured log to last 30 lines (most recent LLM
   calls are the relevant ones)
4. Print the assembled summary with a clear delimiter:
   ```
   ┄┄┄ FAILURE SUMMARY (paste into LLM) ┄┄┄
   ## test_russian_response_quality FAILED
   Error: TimeoutError (120s)
   Log:
     Classifier raw LLM output: 'plan:ru'
     Classifier: plan (lang=ru)
     Briefer for planner: 1 modules, 0 tools
     Plan: goal='...', 5 tasks
     ...
   ┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄┄
   ```

**Files:** `utils/run_tests.sh`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Modify `run_suite()`: capture output to temp file via `tee` while
  preserving live terminal output
- [x] Add `_extract_failure_summary()` function: parses pytest output,
  extracts failure blocks with test name + assertion + captured log
- [x] Filter: keep only `kiso.*` and `HTTP Request` lines from log
- [x] Compress captured log: last 30 lines per failure
- [x] Strip ANSI colors from the summary block (clean text for LLM)
- [x] Print summary at script end when `FAILED=1`, with clear delimiters
- [x] Handle Docker-wrapped tests (pytest output is inside Docker stdout,
  captured by tee)
- [x] Handle multiple failures in same run (concatenate blocks)
- [x] Temp file cleanup on exit (trap EXIT)

---

### M887 — Switch planner fallback model to minimax-m2.7 ✅

**Problem:** The planner fallback model is `gemini-2.5-flash-lite`, a lite
variant that produces lower quality plans. When the primary planner
(deepseek-v3.2) fails after 3 retries, SSE stall, or circuit breaker, the
fallback should be a capable model — not a lite one.

**Approach:** Change `planner_fallback_model` default from
`gemini-2.5-flash-lite` to `minimax/minimax-m2.7` in config.

**Files:** `kiso/config.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `planner_fallback_model` default to `minimax/minimax-m2.7`

---

## Phase 64 — Fix F17: registry visibility after first tool install

**Problem:** F17 (multi-tool pipeline) fails because after the first tool
(browser) is installed, the planner loses visibility of all other registry
tools (ocr, aider, etc.). Three bugs cascade:

1. `_load_registry_hints()` reads `data.get("skills")` but `registry.json`
   uses `"tools"` → `registry_hints` always empty
2. `get_registry_tools()` only called when `not installed` → after first
   tool install, remaining registry tools invisible to planner
3. Module selection (`kiso_native`, `plugin_install`) depends on
   `not installed or registry_text` → neither loaded when any tool installed

Result: planner doesn't know OCR/aider exist as kiso tools, doesn't have
install rules, falls back to general knowledge (`apt-get install tesseract`,
direct exec commands for aider).

---

### M888 — Fix registry_hints key mismatch in sysenv.py ✅

**Problem:** `_load_registry_hints()` (sysenv.py:242) uses
`data.get("skills", [])` but `registry.json` uses `"tools"` as the key.
Registry hints are always empty — the planner never sees tool names/descriptions
in the System Environment section.

**Files:** `kiso/sysenv.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `data.get("skills", [])` → `data.get("tools", [])` at
  sysenv.py:242
- [x] Unit test: `_load_registry_hints()` returns non-empty string when
  `registry.json` exists and has `"tools"` entries
- [x] Unit test: returns empty when no registry.json

---

### M889 — Show uninstalled registry tools regardless of installed count ✅

**Problem:** `brain.py:1210` fetches registry tools only when
`not installed and not is_replan`. After browser install, `installed` is
non-empty → OCR/aider/websearch become invisible to the planner.

`get_registry_tools(installed_names)` already filters out installed tools
and returns empty string when all are installed, so token cost is
self-regulating.

**Approach:** Change condition from `not installed and not is_replan` to
`not is_replan`. This way:
- Fresh instance (0 tools): shows all 8 registry tools (~160 tokens)
- After browser (1 tool): shows 7 remaining (~140 tokens)
- After browser+ocr+aider (3 tools): shows 5 remaining (~100 tokens)
- All installed: returns "" → no extra context, no module forcing

Module selection cascade (Bug 3) fixes itself: with `registry_text`
non-empty, `kiso_native` is forced in briefer path and `plugin_install`
is added in fallback path — both correct behaviors.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `if not installed and not is_replan:` →
  `if not is_replan:` at brain.py:1210
- [x] Update comment to explain: "Show uninstalled registry tools so the
  planner knows what's available for install. Filtered by installed_names,
  so returns empty when all tools are installed."
- [x] Fix 2 tests that assumed registry_text was always empty when tools
  installed: mock `get_registry_tools` to isolate keyword behavior

---

**Problem:** After M888-M889, F17 should work because:
- Planner sees OCR/aider in registry after browser install
- `kiso_native` module loaded → planner knows "in hints → kiso tool install"
- `plugin_install` module available → planner knows exact install commands
- Validation guides planner to use `kiso tool install ocr` instead of

### M891 — Test runner: show elapsed time per suite ✅

**Problem:** No visibility into how long each test suite takes. When
investigating performance regressions or identifying bottlenecks, you
have to manually check timestamps. Especially useful for long suites
(live ~15min, functional ~10min, extended ~15min).

**Approach:** In `run_suite()`, capture `$SECONDS` before and after the
command. Display elapsed time in the pass/fail line:
```
✓ Unit tests: PASSED (92s)
✗ Functional tests: FAILED (487s)
```
Format as `Xs` for <60s, `Xm Ys` for ≥60s.

### M892 — Rename initial plan header "Planning..." → "Thinking..." ✅

**Problem:** When a message arrives, `create_plan()` is called with
`"Planning..."` as the initial header text. This appears in the CLI
before classifier/briefer/planner even start. "Planning" is misleading
because the system is doing much more than planning at that point
(classifying, briefing, planning, executing). "Thinking" better
describes the overall process from the user's perspective.

**Note:** This is NOT about renaming internal phase constants
(`WORKER_PHASE_PLANNING` etc.) — those stay as-is. This only changes
the user-visible plan header string.

## Phase 67 — Fix install_proposal not persisted on replan plans

**Problem:** When the planner generates a plan with `install_proposal=True`
and the plan fails → replans, the replan plan does NOT persist the
`install_proposal` flag to the database. On the next message cycle,
`session_has_install_proposal()` checks the LAST completed plan (the
replan), finds no flag, and returns False. The planner then generates
another install approval message instead of executing the install.

This is the root cause of F1 (browser install flow) and F2 (gazzetta
news) failures: the planner proposes install correctly, but after a
replan cycle the approval state is lost.

Two bugs in the replan path (loop.py ~2340-2368):
1. `install_proposal` not persisted on replan plans (missing
   `update_plan_install_proposal` call)
2. `install_approved` not passed to `run_planner` in the replan path
   (the initial path passes it at line 2571)

---

### M897 — Persist install_proposal on replan plans ✅

**Problem:** `update_plan_install_proposal(db, new_plan_id)` is called
for the initial plan (line 2601) but NOT for replan plans (line 2368).
When a plan with `install_proposal=True` replans, the replan plan
doesn't carry the flag → `session_has_install_proposal()` returns False
on the next message cycle.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] After `_persist_plan_tasks` for replan, add
  `update_plan_install_proposal(db, new_plan_id)` when
  `new_plan.get("install_proposal")` is True
- [x] Add `install_approved` parameter to `_run_planning_loop`, pass it
  from `_process_message` and to `run_planner` in the replan path
- [x] Unit test: replan plan persists install_proposal flag
- [x] Unit test: replan without proposal overrides parent's proposal
- [x] Unit test: multi-replan chain (3 replans) — last plan's
  install_proposal wins, plan without proposal overrides the chain
- [x] Integration test for install_approved in replan path covered by
  F1/F2 functional tests (M898)

## Phase 68 — Force registry tools into planner context

**Problem:** `available_registry_tools` (list of installable tools from
the registry) is added to `context_pool` for the briefer to select, but
is never directly injected into the planner's `context_parts`. The
briefer can (and does) filter it out when it doesn't seem relevant.

Result: when the user asks "extract text using OCR", the planner sees
browser (installed) but has no idea OCR exists as a kiso tool. Falls
back to `exec: tesseract` → fails → stuck. This is the root cause of
F17's OCR step failure.

The `registry_hints` in System Environment (M888 fix) provides tool
names in one line, but the planner needs the full structured list to
make install decisions. Like `safety_facts`, registry tools should be
always-injected, not gated by the briefer.

---

### M899 — Always inject registry tools into planner context ✅

**Problem:** `registry_text` (from `get_registry_tools()`) is only in
`context_pool` — the briefer decides whether to include it. When
filtered out, the planner doesn't know installable tools exist.

**Approach:** After the tools section (brain.py ~line 1380), add
`registry_text` directly to `context_parts` when non-empty. This
bypasses the briefer and ensures the planner always sees what tools
are available for install. Token cost is minimal (~120 tokens for 7
uninstalled tools, self-regulating to 0 when all installed).

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] After the tools section, inject `registry_text` directly into
  `context_parts` as "## Available Tools (not installed)"
- [x] Remove `context_pool["available_registry_tools"]` — no longer
  needed since we inject directly
- [x] Unit test: planner context includes registry tools when uninstalled
- [x] Unit test: no registry section when all tools installed
- [x] Unit test: registry text appears in planner user message

---

### M900 — F17 validation ~~DROPPED~~ (superseded by M905, then M964-M967)

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Run F17:
  `./utils/run_tests.sh s "tests/functional/test_multitool.py::TestF17FullPipeline"`
- [ ] Verify OCR step proposes kiso tool install (not tesseract exec)
- [ ] Verify all 4 steps complete: browser → ocr → aider → exec+msg
- [ ] If still failing, analyze logs and iterate

---

### M901 — Filter needs_install against installed tools ✅

**Problem:** The planner LLM sometimes sets `needs_install: ["browser"]`
even when browser is already installed. `install_proposal` becomes True
unconditionally from `bool(plan.get("needs_install"))` without checking
whether the listed tools are actually uninstalled. This causes the
planner to propose installing a tool that's already available — breaking
the install flow (F17 step 1 failure).

**Approach:** After validation completes and before computing
`install_proposal`, filter `needs_install` to remove tools that are
already in `installed_names`. If the filtered list is empty, set it to
None so the condition is falsy.

This is a structural invariant: "you cannot need_install something
that's already installed." Handles all edge cases:
- Tool not installed → kept in needs_install
- Tool installed → removed
- Tool installed but broken → still removed (repair != install)
- Zero tools installed → skip filter entirely (empty installed_names)
- Mixed → only uninstalled tools remain

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Before `install_proposal` calculation, filter `needs_install`
  against `installed_names` — remove already-installed tools
- [x] Unit test: installed tool removed → install_proposal=False
- [x] Unit test: uninstalled tool preserved → install_proposal=True
- [x] Unit test: mixed → only uninstalled remains

---

### M902 — Remove redundant "Answer in" msg validation ✅

**Problem:** `validate_plan` (brain.py:732-737) rejects plans where
the msg task detail doesn't start with "Answer in {language}.". But
`_msg_task` (loop.py:254-262) already prepends the correct language
prefix at runtime — the validation is redundant.

The validation causes real harm: when the planner's first attempt has
correct tool tasks but a msg without the language prefix, the entire
plan is rejected. On retry, the planner over-corrects → drops tool
tasks → generates msg-only plan → test fails because no work was done.

This is the direct cause of F17 step 1 failure: planner generates
browser tool + msg → rejected for missing "Answer in English." → retry
produces msg-only → no screenshot taken.

**Approach:** Remove the `has_lang_prefix` validation check (lines
732-737). Keep the "empty after prefix" check (lines 738-744) but
make it apply when the prefix IS present, unchanged. `_msg_task`
handles the prefix injection at runtime.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Remove the `has_lang_prefix` check — `_msg_task` handles it at
  runtime
- [x] Generalize "cleaned < 5 chars" check to work with or without
  prefix (strips prefix if present before length check)
- [x] Update 4 tests across test_brain.py and test_messenger_quality.py
- [x] Add M902 tests: no-prefix substantive detail accepted, short
  detail still rejected

---

### M903 — Validation: propose install for registry tools, not exec fallback ✅

**Problem:** When the planner uses an uninstalled tool, the validation
message says:

```
"If the goal can be achieved with built-in task types (search, exec)
or installed tools, use those instead. Only if no alternative exists,
plan a msg asking whether to install."
```

Since `exec` can technically do almost anything, the planner ALWAYS
falls back to exec instead of proposing install. This contradicts the
`kiso_native` module which says "Not installed? Set needs_install,
msg user for approval." Result: tools like aider are never proposed
for install — the planner writes scripts via exec instead.

**Root cause in F17:** planner correctly identifies aider for code
writing (registry says "Code editing, refactoring..."), tries `type=
tool` → validation rejects → planner uses exec → script written
manually → 4 replans → test fails because no aider tool task.

**Approach:** Pass registry tool names to `validate_plan`. If the
uninstalled tool is in the registry, the validation message should
say "propose install" not "use exec instead":

- **In registry:** "Tool X is available in the registry. Plan a msg
  asking whether to install it, then end the plan."
- **Not in registry:** "Tool X is unknown. Use exec or installed
  tools instead."

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] `registry_hint_names` parameter already existed — used it in the
  uninstalled-tool validation check
- [x] Registry tool → "available in the registry, plan msg to install,
  Do NOT fall back to exec"
- [x] Unknown tool → "not in the registry, Remove this tool task, use
  exec or installed tools"
- [x] Unit test: registry tool → propose install message
- [x] Unit test: unknown tool → use alternatives message
- [x] Updated 2 existing tests for new message format

---

## Phase 69 — Docker base tools + F17 validation

**Problem:** The Docker container (`python:3.12-slim`) has almost no
system tools installed. The planner generates commands like `file`,
`jq`, `ps aux`, `tree`, `unzip` from LLM training knowledge, but they
fail with `command not found` → wasted replan cycles.

The container should have a standard set of generalisti tools that any
agent would reasonably need. These are small, universal, and the LLM
already knows how to use them — no prompt changes needed. `PROBE_BINARIES`
in sysenv.py already probes for all of them and reports availability to
the planner via "Installed binaries:" in System Environment.

---

### M904 — Install base system tools in Docker containers ✅

**Problem:** `python:3.12-slim` + `git curl openssh-client` is too
minimal. The planner regularly generates commands that don't exist,
causing `exit 127` failures and replan waste.

**Tools to install (total ~3.7MB):**

| Package | Size | Commands | Why |
|---------|------|----------|-----|
| `file` | 79KB | `file` | Identify file types — planner uses constantly |
| `jq` | 124KB | `jq` | Parse JSON — APIs, configs, registry |
| `unzip` | 387KB | `unzip` | Extract archives from web/datasets |
| `zip` | 627KB | `zip` | Create archives for deliverables |
| `tree` | 129KB | `tree` | Explore directory structure |
| `procps` | 2.4MB | `ps`, `kill`, `uptime`, `top` | Process management, diagnostics |

**Not installing (too heavy or redundant):**
- `wget` (3.8MB) — redundant with `curl`
- `dnsutils` (5MB) — too specific
- `imagemagick` (15MB) — too heavy, better as kiso tool
- `less`, `nano` — interactive, agent uses cat/head/heredoc
- `bc` — Python does math better

**Files:** `Dockerfile`, `Dockerfile.test`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Update `Dockerfile` apt-get: add `jq unzip zip tree procps`
  (`file` already added in prior commit)
- [x] Update `Dockerfile.test` apt-get: same packages
- [x] Add `tree` to `PROBE_BINARIES` in sysenv.py (was missing)
- [x] Build verified: all 6 tools present and functional

### M906 — Skip file-creation validation when plan has needs_install ✅

**Problem:** The validation rule at brain.py:971 checks if the goal
mentions creating a file (verbs like "write"/"create" + nouns like
"file"/"script") and rejects plans without exec/tool tasks. This
conflicts with install proposals: the planner wants to propose
installing aider (msg-only plan) to write word_count.py, but the
validation says "goal mentions a file → needs exec/tool tasks."

The planner can't satisfy both:
1. M903: "aider not installed → plan msg to install"
2. This rule: "goal mentions file → must have exec/tool"

Result: 3 validation retries exhausted → planning fails → aider
never proposed for install. Root cause of F17 step 3 failure.

**Approach:** Add `not has_needs_install` to the condition at line 971.
When `needs_install` is set, the planner is proposing to install a
tool that will create the file in a future plan — the file-creation
check is premature.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `has_needs_install = bool(plan.get("needs_install"))` before
  the file-creation check
- [x] Add `and not has_needs_install` to the condition at line 971
- [x] Unit test: file goal + no exec → rejected (unchanged)
- [x] Unit test: file goal + needs_install → accepted

## Phase 70 — Production diagnostic logging

**Problem:** The current logging is blind in critical paths:

- **Reviewer** logs `Review: status=replan` but NOT the reason. When
  investigating why a plan keeps replanning, we can't see what the
  reviewer thinks is wrong without adding ad-hoc logging.
- **Exec tasks** log output ONLY on failure (exit != 0). When an exec
  succeeds (exit 0) but produces wrong output, the reviewer replans
  and we can't see what the exec actually returned.
- **Tool tasks** same gap — no output logged on success.

These gaps make any production or test debugging require reproducing
the issue with added logging, wasting time. The info should always be
there.

---

### M907 — Log reviewer reason and exec/tool output on success ✅

**Approach:** Small logging additions, no behavior changes:

1. Reviewer: change `log.info("Review: status=%s", status)` to include
   `reason` (truncated to 200 chars, handle None)
2. Exec task: add `log.info` for exit=0 with stdout truncated to 200
   chars (matches the existing failure log pattern)
3. Tool task: same — log output on success

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Reviewer log: add reason to the existing INFO line
  (`(review.get("reason") or "")[:200]` — handles None)
- [x] Exec task: add INFO log on success with stdout[:200]
- [x] Tool task: add INFO+WARNING logs on success/failure with
  stdout[:200]/[:500] (matching exec pattern)
- [x] All 3676 tests pass — no breaks from None reason

## Phase 71 — Worker translator session file awareness

**Problem:** The planner receives `session_files` (list of files in the
workspace from current + previous plans) via `context_pool`. It uses
this to generate exec tasks like "Run word_count.py with ocr-text.txt
as input". But the worker translator that converts this to a shell
command does NOT receive the file listing — it only gets:

1. System Environment (binaries, distro, working dir)
2. Preceding Task Outputs (from the SAME plan only)
3. The task detail text

Without knowing the filesystem layout, the translator generates blind
commands: `find . -name "ocr-text.txt"`, `cat word_count.py` (shows
source instead of running), `python3 word_count.py` (no piped input).
This is the root cause of F17 step 4 failure — 18 replans because the
translator can't construct `cat pub/ocr-text.txt | python3 word_count.py`.

The planner has the info, the translator doesn't. Structural gap.

---

### M908 — Pass session files to worker translator context ✅

**Approach:** In `_handle_exec_task`, compute the session file listing
(same `_list_session_files` the planner uses) and pass it to
`build_exec_translator_messages` as an additional context section
`## Workspace Files`. The translator then knows what files exist and
their paths.

Token cost is minimal — the file listing is typically 3-10 lines. The
information is critical: it turns blind file discovery into direct
path usage.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/worker/loop.py`, `tests/test_worker.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `workspace_files: str = ""` parameter to both
  `build_exec_translator_messages` and `run_exec_translator`
- [x] Add `## Workspace Files` section in context_parts (after sys_env)
- [x] In `_handle_exec_task`, call `_list_session_files(ctx.session)`
  and pass to `run_exec_translator`
- [x] Update worker.md prompt: "Workspace Files: these files exist in
  the working directory. Use exact paths shown — no find or ls needed."
- [x] All 3676 tests pass

---

### M910 — M903 validation: unknown tools → inform user, don't try exec ✅

**Problem:** For tools not in the registry, the validation says "use

commands for tools that don't exist anywhere.

Affects: TestF22NonexistentTool.

### M911 — Language assertion: accept tied scores ✅

**Problem:** `assert_language` uses strict `>` comparison. When a
response mixes target language with technical content (SSH keys, code,
URLs), function-word scores tie → assertion fails.

Affects: TestF3SSHKey.

**Approach:** Change `target > best_other` to `target >= best_other`.
A tie means the target language is equally present — acceptable for
mixed-content responses. General: any response with embedded technical
content will have English function words.

**Files:** `tests/functional/conftest.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `assert target > best_other` to
  `assert target >= best_other` in `assert_language`

---

### M912 — Classifier: known entity priority over system state rule ✅

**Problem:** The classifier prompt has two conflicting rules:
- "hostname, IP, uptime... → plan (requires shell commands)"
- "questions about known entities → chat_kb (no tools needed)"

When hostname IS in Known Entities (boot fact, entity 'self'), both
rules match. The classifier picks "plan" → unnecessary exec task.
This makes the test flaky: sometimes chat_kb (correct), sometimes plan.

**Approach:** Add priority rule to classifier.md line 16: "UNLESS the
value is already available in Known Entities below — then use chat_kb
(the answer is already known, no shell command needed)."

General: any system-state info that's already in facts → chat_kb.
Covers hostname, IP, distro — all saved at boot.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/classifier.md`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add "UNLESS the value is already available in Known Entities →
  chat_kb" exception to the system state rule in classifier.md
- [x] Updated unit test for system state rule to verify Known Entities
  exception is present

---

### M913 — Switch worker translator model to deepseek-v3.2 ✅

**Problem:** The worker translator (gemini-2.5-flash-lite) generates
malformed shell commands ~20% of the time — labels (`ls: /path`),
markdown (`` `ls` ``), prompt markers (`$ ls`). The prompt says
"Output ONLY shell commands" but the model violates this.

The translator is the one role where output format is critical: it
must produce pure shell, nothing else. gemini-flash-lite is too
unreliable for this.

**Approach:** Change the worker model default from
`gemini-2.5-flash-lite` to `deepseek/deepseek-v3.2` in config.py.
deepseek-v3.2 is already used for planner and messenger — it follows
strict format instructions correctly.

Cost impact: negligible. Translator input ~400 tokens, output ~50
tokens. Even at deepseek pricing, this is cents per thousand calls.

**Files:** `kiso/config.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `"worker": "google/gemini-2.5-flash-lite"` to
  `"worker": "deepseek/deepseek-v3.2"` in MODEL_DEFAULTS
- [x] Updated config template comment

## Phase 73 — Functional test fixes (F1, F17, F22, F23, F31)

### M914 — F1: assert_language strips quoted content ✅

**Problem:** `assert_language` strips code blocks but not blockquotes
or list items. When the messenger translates example.com content to
Italian, it quotes the English page text (blockquotes `> ...`, lists
`- ...`), inflating the English function-word score (16) above the
Italian score (11).

`_strip_quoted_content()` already exists and handles this — used by
`assert_no_failure_language` but not by `assert_language`.

**Approach:** Use `_strip_quoted_content(cleaned)` in `assert_language`
before scoring function words. General: any test where the response
cites foreign-language content won't trigger false positives.

**Files:** `tests/functional/conftest.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `cleaned = _strip_quoted_content(cleaned)` before the
  function-word scoring loop in `assert_language`

### M915 — F31: change language test questions to pure knowledge ✅

**Problem:** All language response tests (F19/F20/F31/F32) ask "What
are the 3 most popular programming languages?" — the classifier can
legitimately route this as `plan` (popularity changes over time →
research needed). When routed as plan, the planner tries browsing
PYPL → browser can't extract table → replan loop → timeout.

The PURPOSE of these tests is validating language detection + response
quality, not research capability.

**Approach:** Change the question to something that's unambiguously
general knowledge: "What is recursion in programming? Explain with a
simple example." This is clearly chat/chat_kb — no tool needed. Change
for all 4 language tests (EN/ES/RU/ZH) for consistency. Update
assertions: check for recursion-related keywords instead of language
names.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_core_flows.py`

**Tasks:**

  Explain with a simple example" (English), update keyword assertions
- [x] Change F20 question to Spanish equivalent, update keyword
  assertions

  assertions, reduce timeout to 120s
- [x] Change F32 question to Chinese equivalent, update keyword
  assertions

---

### M916 — F17: OCR tool reliability (temperature + retry) ✅

**Problem:** The OCR tool (`plugins/tool-ocr/run.py`) calls
`google/gemini-2.5-flash-lite` via OpenRouter without setting
`temperature` (defaults to model default ~0.7-1.0) and with zero
retry logic. When the API returns empty `choices` or empty `content`,
the tool outputs "No text detected" even for trivial pages like
example.com. This causes F17 step 2 to fail and cascade through the
pipeline.

F17 is a real-API test (not mocked) — these changes directly affect
test reliability. `_call_gemini()` is called by exactly 2 functions:
`do_extract` (OCR) and `do_describe` (image description). Both
benefit from deterministic output. Existing unit tests mock
`httpx.post` and don't inspect payload — no test breakage.

**Approach:** Two changes to `_call_gemini()`:
1. Add `"temperature": 0` to the API payload. Both callers (extract
   and describe) benefit from deterministic output — extract is OCR
   (should be deterministic), describe needs consistency not creativity.
2. Add retry on empty response: if `choices` is empty or `content` is
   empty string, retry up to 2 times with 1s/2s backoff. Only retry
   on empty, not on HTTP errors (already raises RuntimeError).

Temperature:0 alone is NOT sufficient — "sometimes returns empty"
(per memory notes) indicates transient API failures, not just
randomness. Retry handles those.

**Files:** `plugins/tool-ocr/run.py`, `plugins/tool-ocr/tests/test_run.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `"temperature": 0` to payload in `_call_gemini`
- [x] Add retry loop (max 2 retries, 1s/2s backoff) on empty
  choices/content in `_call_gemini`
- [x] Add unit test for retry exhaustion (mock returns empty 3 times)
- [x] Add unit test for retry success (empty first, success on retry)

---

### M916b — Transcriber tool: same temperature + retry fix ✅

**Problem:** The transcriber tool (`plugins/tool-transcriber/run.py`)
has the exact same pattern as the OCR tool: calls
`gemini-2.5-flash-lite` via OpenRouter with no temperature setting and
no retry logic. Outputs "No speech detected in audio" on empty
response.

**Approach:** Apply the same fix as M916: `temperature: 0` + retry
on empty response (max 2, 1s/2s backoff). Same rationale applies —
transcription is deterministic, transient failures need retry.

Also changed: empty `choices` array no longer raises RuntimeError —
now treated as empty response (retried, then returns "").

**Files:** `plugins/tool-transcriber/run.py`,
`plugins/tool-transcriber/tests/test_run.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `"temperature": 0` to payload in transcriber's Gemini call
- [x] Add retry loop (max 2 retries, 1s/2s backoff) on empty response
- [x] Add unit test for retry exhaustion + retry success

---

### M917 — F22: fix search validation message contradiction ✅

**Problem:** When a search task matches plugin discovery, the
validation error says: "use an exec task with `curl <registry_url>`
instead". But the planner prompt (line 114) says: "Do NOT curl for
names absent from registry_hints." The validation message contradicts
the prompt, and since it's the most recent context, the planner
follows it — curling for nonexistent tools → replan loop → timeout.

The circular replan detection WOULD catch this eventually (66.7% word
overlap between replan reasons, 100% strategy fingerprint), but the
timeout (180s) arrives first because each plan cycle takes ~60s
(3 reviewer retries × exec + LLM calls).

**Approach:** Change the search validation error message to be
consistent with the planner prompt. Include both cases:
- If tool name is in registry_hints → use curl to discover details
- If tool name is NOT in hints → plan a msg task informing the user

No code logic changes — only the error message string. The validation
still rejects search for plugin discovery; it just gives better
guidance on what to do instead.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Update the search plugin discovery validation error message to
  include both registry-present and registry-absent guidance
- [x] Existing unit tests pass (substring match compatible)
- [x] Fix assert_language: require target > 0 (empty/numbers-only
  text was passing with 0 >= 0 after _strip_quoted_content change)

### M918 — F23: add "manage knowledge" to classifier plan category ✅

**Problem:** The classifier prompt's `plan` category lists actions:
"file ops, code, search, install, run, configure, navigate, system
introspection, manage tools/connectors/plugins." Knowledge storage
("ricordati che X", "remember that X") is missing. The planner HAS
`kiso knowledge add` as a tool, so this IS a plan action.

Without this, the classifier matches "ricordati che il progetto
Artemis usa PostgreSQL" as `chat_kb` (sees entity/fact reference)
instead of `plan` (knowledge storage action). Result: fast path →
messenger → nothing saved → cross-session knowledge broken.

This is a **deterministic structural bug**, not flakiness — 4 tests
are affected: F10 (TestMultiTurnLearning), F15
(TestF15EntityDedupTagReuse), F23 (TestF23CrossSessionKnowledge),
F26 (TestF26TeachFactThenRecall). All use "ricordati che X" and
all fail the same way.

**Approach:** Add "manage knowledge" to the plan category's action
list in classifier.md. Language-agnostic: covers "ricordati che",
"remember that", "запомни что", "记住" etc. Does NOT affect knowledge
queries ("what do you know about X?" / "ti ricordi X?") which remain
chat_kb — those are retrieval, not storage.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/classifier.md`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add "manage knowledge" to the plan category action list in
  classifier.md
- [x] Add unit test verifying "manage knowledge" present in
  classifier system prompt

for pytest's "short test summary" lines (`FAILED tests/path::Class::test`),
collect the test node IDs, and print a rerun snippet:
```
━━━ RERUN FAILED TESTS ━━━
./utils/run_tests.sh s "tests/functional/test_core_flows.py::TestF31 tests/functional/test_browser.py::TestF1BrowserNavigate"
```

Use the "short test summary info" section which pytest always emits —
lines matching `^FAILED (.+)$`. Join all paths into a single `s`
command.

**Files:** `utils/run_tests.sh`

**Tasks:**

- [x] Deduplicates repeated test IDs, strips pytest reason suffixes

---

### M920 — Registry hints from online fetch, not local file ✅

**Problem:** `_load_registry_hints()` in sysenv.py reads
`registry.json` from the local filesystem (`Path(__file__).parent.parent`).
But `registry.py:fetch_registry()` fetches the same data from GitHub
(cached 5min). These are two independent paths to the same data.

In Docker containers the local file doesn't exist (Dockerfile.test
copies `kiso/`, `cli/`, `tests/` but not `registry.json`) →
`_load_registry_hints()` returns `""` → `_reg_hint_names = None` →
`validate_plan` falls into M910 ("tool not in registry") for ALL
tools, even though the planner knows they exist (via
`get_registry_tools` which uses the online fetch).

This is the root cause of F17 step 3 failing: the planner puts aider
in `needs_install` (knows it from GitHub fetch), but validation says
"aider not in registry" (local file missing).

**Approach:** Make `_load_registry_hints()` use
`registry.fetch_registry()` instead of reading the local file.
`fetch_registry()` already has a 5-minute TTL cache, so this adds
no extra network calls (it's already called by `get_registry_tools`
a few lines earlier in `run_planner`).

The local `registry.json` file stays in the repo (it IS the source
that GitHub serves), but nothing should read it directly at runtime.

**Chain of changes:**
1. `sysenv._load_registry_hints()` → call `fetch_registry()` instead
   of reading local file
2. Remove the `Path(__file__).parent.parent / "registry.json"` read
3. Update unit tests that mock the local file read

**Files:** `kiso/sysenv.py`, `tests/test_sysenv.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change `_load_registry_hints()` to use `fetch_registry()` from
  `kiso.registry` instead of reading the local file
- [x] Update unit tests: mock `kiso.registry.fetch_registry` instead
  of patching filesystem Path

---

right after building `installed_names` and `_reg_hint_names`, logging

Temporary diagnostic — remove after F17 root cause is identified.

### M923 — Log tool task stderr for successful tasks ✅

**Problem:** The OCR tool writes diagnostic info to stderr
(`[ocr-diag] Empty response: {model, choices_len, finish_reason}`),
but `_handle_tool_task` in loop.py only logs stderr for FAILED tasks
(line 1201-1204). For successful tasks (exit 0 + empty text still
counts as "done"), stderr is saved to DB but not logged.

This makes it impossible to see the diagnostic output in the test
failure summary.

**Approach:** Add `log.info` for stderr when it's non-empty, even
for successful tool tasks.

- [x] In `_handle_tool_task`, log stderr when non-empty for ok tasks

### M924 — OCR: fix thinking parameter for gemini-2.5-flash ✅

**Problem:** gemini-2.5-flash has built-in thinking. The model uses
part of `max_tokens` (4096) for reasoning before responding. If the
reasoning budget consumes most tokens, the final content is empty.

First attempt used `"reasoning": {"effort": "none"}` — but `"none"`
is NOT a valid OpenRouter value (valid: `"low"`, `"medium"`, `"high"`).
The parameter was silently ignored, thinking stayed active at default
effort, and OCR kept returning empty.

**Approach:** Change to `"reasoning": {"effort": "low"}` (uses ~20%
of tokens for reasoning) + increase max_tokens from 4096 to 8192 as
safety margin. For simple OCR text extraction, low reasoning + 8192
tokens guarantees enough room for content.

**Files:** `plugins/tool-ocr/run.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] ~~First attempt: effort "none"~~ (invalid value, silently ignored)
- [x] Fix: change to `"reasoning": {"effort": "low"}`
- [x] Increase max_tokens from 4096 to 8192

---

### M925 — Fix F17 step 2 false positive assertion ✅

**Problem:** The step 2 OCR assertion joins ALL task outputs from
ALL plans in the session:
```python
ocr_output = " ".join(
    t.get("output", "") or "" for t in r2.tasks
    if t.get("status") == "done"
).lower()
assert "example" in ocr_output
```

`r2.tasks` includes msg tasks from prior plans that mention "example"
(e.g., "I'll extract text from the example.com screenshot"). The
assertion passes even when the OCR tool returns empty text — it's
been a false positive all along.

**Approach:** Filter to only OCR tool task outputs from the current
plan result, not all session tasks. Check that a `type: tool` task
with `tool: ocr` exists and its output contains "example".

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_multitool.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Fix step 2 assertion to check only OCR tool task output
  (filter by type=tool + plan_id=last plan)
- [x] Add explicit check that OCR tool tasks exist in last plan

### M926 — Remove M922 diagnostic logging ✅

**Problem:** M922 added temporary `log.info("Planner tool visibility: ...")`
for debugging. The root cause is identified (registry hints + thinking
tokens). The diagnostic can be removed.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Remove M922 diagnostic log.info from `run_planner`

### M927 — Show per-test duration inline in pytest output ✅

**Problem:** pytest `-v` shows `PASSED [ 5%]` but no per-test
duration. For live/functional tests that take seconds to minutes,
it's useful to see how long each test took inline, not just in a
summary table at the end.

**Approach:** Add a `pytest_runtest_makereport` hook in the root
`conftest.py` that appends the call duration to the nodeid suffix.
When `-v` is active, pytest shows `test_name (1.6s) PASSED [100%]`
instead of `test_name PASSED [100%]`. Only shows duration for tests
taking ≥0.1s to avoid clutter on fast unit tests. Formats as
`Xm Ys` for ≥60s, `X.Xs` otherwise.

**Files:** `tests/conftest.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `pytest_runtest_makereport` hook that appends duration
  to the test report nodeid for tests ≥0.1s

---

### M928 — Lower circular replan detection threshold ✅

**Problem:** `_detect_circular_replan` uses `> 0.6` (60%) word
overlap threshold for reviewer reasons. But reviewer reasons are
LLM-generated and non-deterministic — the same underlying problem
gets phrased differently each time, resulting in 50-66% overlap
that sometimes misses the threshold. This causes F22 and F21 to
timeout instead of detecting stuck state.

Strategy fingerprint (Jaccard > 0.5 on task structure) is a second
detection layer but fires independently. The word overlap is the
primary detector and needs to be less strict.

**Approach:** Lower threshold from `> 0.6` to `>= 0.5`. Two
replans sharing half their vocabulary in the failure reason are
almost certainly circular. False positives are guarded by: minimum
2 history entries + strategy fingerprint as secondary confirmation.

**Files:** `kiso/worker/loop.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Change word overlap threshold from `> 0.6` to `>= 0.5` in
  `_detect_circular_replan`
- [x] Add unit test for 50% boundary detection

---

### M929 — Planner: built-in search always sufficient when tool not installed ✅

**Problem:** The planner prompt says "Built-in search for simple
lookups; search tool for detailed research." This false distinction
makes the planner prefer websearch tool (which needs installing)
over the built-in `type: search` (which uses perplexity/sonar and
works immediately). Result: planner proposes installing websearch
instead of using built-in search. Affects F7 and SearchTask tests.

**Approach:** Replace the simple/detailed distinction with: "Built-in
search handles all web queries. Prefer installed search tool when
available." This way:
- No tools installed → built-in search, always
- Websearch installed → prefer it (richer output)
- No false choice when tool isn't available

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `tests/test_brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Update planner prompt line 56: "Built-in search handles all
  web queries. Prefer installed search tool when available."
- [x] Update web module line 69: consistent guidance
- [x] No unit tests assert on old search text

---

### M930 — F1 screenshot: follow_redirects in assert_url_reachable ✅

**Problem:** `assert_url_reachable()` in conftest uses the ASGI
client without `follow_redirects=True`, while the fallback path
(no client) does follow redirects. URL `/pub/screenshot.png`
returns 307 redirect to `/pub/{token}/screenshot.png` → test fails
with status 307 instead of 200.

**Approach:** Add `follow_redirects=True` to the `client.get()`
call. Consistent with the no-client path.

**Files:** `tests/functional/conftest.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add `follow_redirects=True` to `client.get(url)` in
  `assert_url_reachable`

### M931 — Always force kiso_native + knowledge storage ~~DROPPED~~ (superseded: M963 install context + M968 knowledge field)

**Problem:** Three failures (F23, apt/timg, F17) share a common
root cause: the briefer strips essential modules from the planner
prompt, and the fallback logic doesn't compensate.

- **apt/timg:** `kiso_native` (install flow) not forced when
  `registry_text` is empty (system packages aren't in registry).
  The planner lacks the expanded install guidance and over-investigates.
- **F23:** `kiso_commands` (where `kiso knowledge add` lives) is
  excluded because `_KISO_CMD_KEYWORDS` doesn't match "ricordati".
  The planner never sees the command → treats "remember" as
  "acknowledge".

**Approach (2 changes):**

1. Force `kiso_native` for ALL plan messages (not just when
   `registry_text` is non-empty). It's 5 lines of install/tool flow
   guidance that's always relevant. Negligible prompt cost.

2. Add knowledge storage mapping to `kiso_native`:
   `User asks to remember/store a fact → kiso knowledge add "text"`.
   Since `kiso_native` is always forced, the planner always knows
   about knowledge storage without needing the full `kiso_commands`
   module. Not a multilingual keyword heuristic — it's a capability
   description in the always-included module.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/roles/planner.md`,
`tests/test_brain.py`, `tests/test_prompts.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] In `build_planner_messages`: force `kiso_native` unconditionally
  (remove the `if not installed or registry_text` condition)
- [ ] In planner.md `kiso_native` module: add knowledge storage line
- [ ] Update affected unit tests

### M932 — Full tool info when briefer returns 0 tools ~~DROPPED~~ (superseded: M971 briefer→flash, M964 diagnostics)

**Problem:** When the briefer returns 0 tools, the fallback path
(brain.py line 1384) injects only the BRIEF tool list (name +
one-line description). But the M824 override (line 1371) would
inject FULL tool info (args_schema, usage_guide). Without
args_schema, the planner can't generate proper tool task args →
falls back to exec. This causes F17 step 3 to use exec instead
of `type: tool, tool: aider`.

**Approach:** When briefer returns 0 tools AND `len(installed) <=
tool_filter_threshold` (default 10), inject full tool info (same
as M824 path). The planner already sees tools in the brief list —
this just adds the detail needed to call them correctly. No risk
of over-use; more info = better tool usage.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`

**Tasks:**
- [ ] Change M824 condition to inject full tool info when installed
  count is under threshold, regardless of briefer tool selection
- [ ] Update affected unit tests

## Phase 74 — Context Intelligence Fixes: File Awareness + Prompt Correctness

Root-cause analysis of a screenshot → OCR flow revealed several
structural issues where LLM roles receive context that is
incomplete, contradictory, or bloated — causing deterministic
hallucinations, wasted replans, and file-not-found errors on
trivially simple tasks. These are not model capability issues:
Gemini 2.5 Flash and DeepSeek v3.2 produce wrong outputs because
the prompts make the correct output impossible.

### M933 — Inject session_files and last_plan into planner prompt ✅ <!-- done -->

**Problem:** M825 adds `session_files` and M823 adds `last_plan`
to `context_pool`, and M825 force-loads the `session_files` module
(which contains the RULES about using local paths). But neither
key appears in `_CONTEXT_POOL_SECTIONS` (brain.py L1543-1557), so:

1. `build_briefer_messages` never renders them — the briefer never
   sees file listings or previous plan results.
2. `build_planner_messages` (briefer path L1310-1316) never injects
   them — the planner gets the RULES ("never re-download a local
   file") but never the DATA (which files exist).

The planner has rules about files it can't see. Result: it creates
download tasks for files already in the workspace, passes filenames
without subdirectory prefix to tool args, and triggers cascading
failures (wrong URLs, file not found, replan loops).

Note: `_collect_workspace_files` in sysenv.py (L404) does put a
compact file listing inside system_env, but it's buried in ~30
lines of OS/binary/CLI info — insufficient for file-centric tasks.

**Approach:**

1. Add `("session_files", "Session Workspace")` and
   `("last_plan", "Previous Plan")` to `_CONTEXT_POOL_SECTIONS`
   so the briefer sees them and can produce better context synthesis.
2. In `build_planner_messages`, inject session_files and last_plan
   as dedicated `##` sections in BOTH the briefer path and the
   fallback path — not gated by briefer output. These are
   operational data (like system_env), not background context.
3. In the `session_files` module of planner.md, change "reference
   by absolute path" to "reference by path as shown in Session
   Workspace listing" — the OCR tool's file_path arg is relative
   to workspace, not absolute.

Cost: ~100-200 extra tokens when files/last_plan exist. Zero
overhead for empty sessions. Guaranteed file awareness.

**Files:** `kiso/brain.py`, `kiso/roles/planner.md`,
`tests/test_brain.py`, `tests/test_prompts.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add session_files and last_plan to `_CONTEXT_POOL_SECTIONS`
- [x] In briefer path (after L1316): inject `## Session Workspace`
  from `context_pool["session_files"]` when present
- [x] In briefer path (after session_files): inject
  `## Previous Plan` from `context_pool["last_plan"]` when present
- [x] In fallback path (after L1346): same two injections
- [x] In planner.md session_files module: change "absolute path"
  to "path as shown in Session Workspace listing"
- [x] Unit tests: verify session_files and last_plan appear in
  planner messages when present (both briefer and fallback paths)
- [x] Unit tests: verify they DON'T appear when empty

---

### M934 — Eliminate msg-first plans (prevent announce hallucination) ✅

**Problem:** The planning_rules module (planner.md L44) says:
"Multi-step plans: insert intermediate msg tasks every 4–5 tasks."

The planner interprets this as: put a msg as the FIRST task to
announce upcoming steps. The detail becomes:
"Briefly tell the user what the system is about to do. Steps:
tool: Navigate to..., tool: Take a screenshot..."

The messenger receives this and faces an irreconcilable conflict:
- messenger.md L8: "Never describe what you WILL do next"
- messenger.md L13: "Never fabricate information not in task outputs"
- messenger.md L15: "Never claim actions unsupported by task outputs"

But the task detail asks it to describe future actions. The model
resolves the conflict by hallucinating that steps already completed
— inventing file paths (sandbox:/mnt/data/screenshot.png), fake
downloads, and non-existent URLs. This happens deterministically:
ANY model would fail because the prompt is self-contradictory.

**Approach:** Rewrite planning_rules L44-45 to make the rule
unambiguous:

```
- The first task must be exec, tool, search, or replan — never msg.
  Intermediate msg tasks report results from already-completed
  tasks only. Never describe upcoming steps or announce the plan.
  For plans with 8+ tasks: one intermediate msg after every 5
  completed exec/tool/search tasks. Shorter plans need only the
  final msg.
```

This preserves intermediate msgs for long plans (webhook/API users
need progress updates) while eliminating the announce pattern.

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `tests/test_prompts.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Rewrite planning_rules L44-45 with the new msg-ordering rule
- [x] Add prompt unit test: verify the "first task must be" and
  "never describe upcoming" text is present in planning_rules

---

### M935 — Planner detail/expect consistency rule ✅

**Problem:** The planner generates task detail and expect that
contradict each other. Example:
- detail: "Navigate and list interactive elements"
- expect: "Page loads successfully"

The reviewer oscillates: first judges by detail (replan — elements
not listed), then by expect on retry (ok — page loaded). This
wastes a retry cycle. The reviewer prompt already says "Sole
criterion is expect" but the model is confused by contradictory
detail.

**Approach:** Add to planning_rules, after the `expect` rule (L35):

```
- detail and expect must be consistent — expect is the ONLY
  criterion the reviewer checks. Don't add goals to detail
  that aren't reflected in expect.
```

**Files:** `kiso/roles/planner.md`, `tests/test_prompts.py`

**Tasks:**
- [x] Add detail/expect consistency rule after L35
- [x] Prompt unit test: verify the rule text is present

---

### M936 — E2E test: screenshot → OCR cross-plan pipeline ✅

**Problem:** No functional test covers the full flow: take
screenshot in plan 1, OCR the screenshot in plan 2 (same session).
The bugs found in this analysis (file paths lost, announce
hallucination, OCR file-not-found) were never caught because no
test exercises this cross-plan file handoff.

**Approach:** Functional test (suite 7) that sends two messages
in the same session:

1. "take a screenshot of example.com" → verifies screenshot file
   exists in pub/, published URL is reachable
2. "use OCR to extract text from the screenshot" → verifies OCR
   receives correct relative path (pub/...), extracts some text,
   no replan triggered

Assertions:
- Plan 1: first task is NOT type "msg" (no announce)
- Plan 1: no replan triggered (task count matches plan)
- Plan 2: planner does NOT create download/curl tasks (file is
  local)
- Plan 2: OCR tool task args contain "pub/" prefix
- Plan 2: OCR succeeds (non-empty text output)
- Plan 2: no replan triggered
- Both: messenger output does not contain "sandbox:" or
  "/mnt/data/" (hallucination markers)

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_cross_plan_files.py`,
`tests/functional/conftest.py` (if new helpers needed)

**Tasks:**
- [x] Create test file with the two-message flow
- [x] Assert no msg-first task in either plan
- [x] Assert no download tasks in OCR plan (file is local)
- [x] Assert messenger output is grounded (no hallucination markers)
- [x] Assert OCR returns non-empty text
- Note: functional+extended test, needs manual run with `./run_tests.sh 8`
